2:26:1651:0:14:72:382:700:12:Times:12:Times:?:A Mechanism Design Approach to Identification and Estimation
2:27:1711:14:14:72:266:686:12:Times:12:Times:?:Bradley Larsen and Anthony Lee Zhang
2:28:1747:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:?:NBER Working Paper No. 24837
2:29:1775:14:14:72:119:658:12:Times:12:Times:?:July 2018
2:30:1784:14:28:72:198:644:12:Times:12:Times:?:JEL No. C1,C7,D4,D8,L0
2:31:1806:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:32:1814:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:?:This  paper  presents  a  two-step  identification  argument  for  a  large  class  of  quasilinear  utility 
2:33:1923:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:?:trading games,  imputing  agents'  values  using  revealed  preference  based  on  their  choices  from  a 
2:34:2029:14:14:72:542:560:12:Times:12:Times:?:convex menu of expected outcomes available in equilibrium. This generalizes many existing two-
2:35:2122:14:14:71:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:?:step  approaches in  the  auctions  literature  and  applies  to  many  cases  for  which  there  are  no 
2:36:2227:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:?:existing tools and where the econometrician may not know the precise rules of the game, such as 
2:37:2322:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:?:incomplete-information bargaining settings. We also derive a methodology for settings in which 
2:38:2416:14:14:71:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:?:agents' actions are not perfectly observed, bounding menus and agents' utilities based on features 
2:39:2514:14:14:71:545:490:12:Times:12:Times:?:of  the  data  that  shift  agents'  imperfectly  observed actions.   We  propose  nonparametric  value 
2:40:2617:14:14:72:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:?:estimation  procedures  based  on  our  identification  results for  general  trading  games.  Our 
2:41:2715:14:14:72:546:462:12:Times:12:Times:?:procedures can be combined with previously existing tools for handling unobserved heterogeneity 
2:42:2810:14:14:72:545:448:12:Times:12:Times:?:and non-independent types. We apply our results to analyze efficiency and surplus division in the 
2:43:2907:14:14:72:545:434:12:Times:12:Times:?:complex  game  played  at  wholesale  used-car  auctions,  that  of  a  secret  reserve price  auction 
2:44:3009:14:42:72:407:420:12:Times:12:Times:?:followed by sequential bargaining between the seller and high bidder.
2:45:3078:42:14:72:146:378:12:Times:12:Times:?:Bradley Larsen
2:46:3092:14:14:72:198:364:12:Times:12:Times:?:Department of Economics
2:47:3115:14:14:72:167:350:12:Times:12:Times:?:Stanford University
2:48:3134:14:14:72:144:336:12:Times:12:Times:?:579 Serra Mall
2:49:3148:14:14:72:169:322:12:Times:12:Times:?:Stanford, CA 94305
2:50:3166:14:14:72:124:308:12:Times:12:Times:?:and NBER
2:51:3174:14:28:72:181:294:12:Times:12:Times:?:bjlarsen@stanford.edu
2:52:3195:28:14:72:169:266:12:Times:12:Times:?:Anthony Lee Zhang
2:53:3212:14:14:72:211:252:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:?:Graduate School of Business
2:54:3239:14:14:72:167:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?:Stanford University
2:55:3258:14:14:72:152:224:12:Times:12:Times:?:655 Knight Way
2:56:3272:14:14:72:169:210:12:Times:12:Times:?:Stanford, CA 94305
2:57:3290:14:0:72:187:196:12:Times:12:Times:?:anthonyz@stanford.edu
3:58:3379:0:27:251:339:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f6:?:1.Introduction
3:59:3393:27:17:91:511:661:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:A frequent goal of the growing empirical literature studying mechanism and market design
3:60:3481:17:17:79:511:644:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is to compare outcomes of a mechanism that is used in practice to outcomes under a theo-
3:61:3569:17:17:79:511:627:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:retical counterfactual benchmark, such as some benchmark notion of efficiency, optimality,
3:62:3659:17:17:79:511:610:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:or equity.  In order to make such counterfactual comparisons, the econometrican must first
3:63:3749:17:16:79:511:593:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimate primitives (principally, distributions of players’ valuations) under the mechanism
3:64:3840:16:17:79:511:577:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:used in practice. Given advances in the methodological literature over the past twenty years,
3:65:3933:17:17:79:511:560:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:such an exercise is straightforward for certain types of real-world mechanisms, such as first
3:66:4026:17:17:79:511:543:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:price auctions.  A number of games observed in the real world, however, are quite complex
3:67:4115:17:17:79:511:526:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and do not have clear-cut equilibrium characterizactions from which the researcher can infer
3:68:4207:17:17:79:511:509:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:valuations with off-the-shelf tools.  Examples of such complex incomplete-information trad-
3:69:4298:17:16:79:511:492:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ing games include alternating-offer bargaining games, simultaneous-move bargaining games,
3:70:4387:16:17:79:511:476:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:non-standard auctions (such as median-price or average-price auctions), auctions preceded
3:71:4476:17:17:79:511:459:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:by a knockout auction (as in cases of collusion), and auctions followed by bargaining (or
3:72:4565:17:17:79:511:442:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the  reverse).   In  such  settings,  analytically  solving  for  equilibria  is  difficult,  and  general
3:73:4671:17:20:79:367:425:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:proposals for identification and estimation have been scarce.
3:74:4732:20:17:91:511:405:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:The theoretical mechanism design literature tackles analysis of such games by abstracting
3:75:4821:17:17:79:511:388:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:away  from  the  particular  rules  of  the  game  or  extensive  form  of  the  game  and  instead
3:76:4920:17:17:79:511:371:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:focusing  on  the  direct  mechanism  corresponding  to  an  equilibrium  of  the  original  game
3:77:5017:17:17:79:511:354:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(following the celebrated Revelation Principle, Myerson 1979).  In this paper, we adopt a
3:78:5106:17:17:79:511:337:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:similar approach for empirical analysis, abstracting away from the rules or extensive form
3:79:5196:17:16:79:511:320:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of  the  game  and  instead  focusing  on  revealed  preference  arguments  to  develop  a  unified
3:80:5295:16:21:79:492:304:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:approach to identification and estimation of players’ valuations in such trading games.
3:81:5382:21:17:91:511:283:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We  focus  on  a  class  of  single-unit,  transferable  utility  trading  games  in  which  players
3:82:5482:17:17:79:511:266:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:have independent private values and their utilities are linear in these values.  This nests a
3:83:5575:17:16:79:511:249:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:number of games, such as various kinds of auctions and bargaining games.  In such a setting,
3:84:5667:16:17:79:510:233:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a player with valuationvwho plays actiona(such an action could be a bid in an auction
3:85:5752:17:17:79:511:216:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:or an offer in bargaining) receives an expected payoff ofvP(a) −T(a), whereP(a)is the
3:86:5837:17:17:79:511:199:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:probability of winning the good andT(a)is the transfer paid by the player in expectation
3:87:5925:17:17:79:510:182:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:when choosing actiona.  Our identification argument is simple:  An agent’s action can be
3:88:6013:17:17:79:511:165:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:considered to be a choice from a convex menu of possible(P,T)pairs, and subgradients of
3:89:6100:17:16:79:511:148:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:this menu provide bounds on the agents value.  When the action space is continuous, the
3:90:6187:16:17:79:511:132:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:derivative of this menu, evaluated at the action chosen by the agent, corresponds precisely
3:91:6278:17:17:79:511:115:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to the agent’s value.  The data requirements for identifying an agent’s value are thus that
3:92:6369:17:17:79:511:98:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the econometrician observe the final allocation,  the final transfer,  and the agent’s action
3:93:6462:17:0:79:510:81:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f8:B:from many independent instances of the same underlying game; the objectsP(·)andT(·)
4:94:6562:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:are  then  essentially  observed  in  the  data,  and  subgradients  of  the  menu  identify  agents’
4:95:6663:17:21:79:111:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:values.
4:96:6670:21:16:91:511:650:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:This is a simple revealed preference argument, and it is by no means new to the theoretical
4:97:6761:16:17:79:511:634:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mechanism design literature.  The novelty of our paper is to exploit this argument to obtain
4:98:6853:17:17:79:511:617:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a general identification—and accompanying estimation—approach that applies to a broad
4:99:6938:17:17:79:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:class  of  games  regardless  of  the  specific  rules  of  the  game,  which  is  applicable  even  in
4:100:7041:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:cases where the econometrician may be unaware of the actual rules of the game, such as
4:101:7127:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:when  prices  arise  from  some  unknown  negotiation  process.   Furthermore,  our  approach
4:102:7220:17:17:79:511:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:can apply to games in which, even if the rules are known, equilibrium outcomes may not
4:103:7306:17:16:79:511:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:be uniquely predicted by the model (due to the possibility of multiple equilibria) or may
4:104:7395:16:17:79:511:516:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:simply be difficult to characterize analytically.  Each of these features of our approach are
4:105:7488:17:17:79:511:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:not particularly advantageous in a well-understood setting such as a first price auctions,
4:106:7578:17:17:79:511:482:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:where the theoretical model has a unique, simple-to-characterize equilibrium and where the
4:107:7668:17:17:79:511:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:rules of the game are known.  In a number of other settings, however, our approach can be
4:108:7757:17:20:79:113:448:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f4:B:useful.1
4:109:7765:20:17:91:511:428:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:A  particular  novel  feature  of  this  paper  is  the  application  of  these  identification  and
4:110:7865:17:17:79:511:411:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimation concepts to cases where actions are imperfectly observed by the econometrician.
4:111:7955:17:17:79:511:394:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:This can include settings where only a portion of an agent’s actions are observed, such as a
4:112:8047:17:16:79:511:377:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:multistage auction mechanism where the econometrician observes an indicative (first-stage)
4:113:8137:16:17:79:511:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:bid  and  the  final  allocation  and  price,  but  not  intermediate-stage  actions;  or  a  bilateral
4:114:8240:17:17:79:511:344:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:bargaining setting where the econometrician may observe a seller’s list price and an indicator
4:115:8334:17:17:79:511:327:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:for whether or not a sale occurs and (if a sale does occur) the final negotiated price, but
4:116:8425:17:17:79:511:310:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:not the full sequence of intermediate bargaining actions.  The imperfectly observed action
4:117:8515:17:17:79:511:293:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:case can also include cases where the action is not observed at all but the econometrician
4:118:8605:17:17:79:511:276:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:observes a variable in the data that is correlated with that agent’s action and not with other
4:119:8699:17:16:79:511:259:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:agents’ actions, similar to an instrumental variable.  We provide conditions under which our
4:120:8791:16:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:identification and estimation approach can be used to approximate equilibrium menus and
4:121:8878:17:21:79:508:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:players’ values, and we provide conditions under which this approximation will work well.
4:122:8967:21:16:91:511:205:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We derive nonparametric estimation procedures to accompany these identification argu-
4:123:9052:16:17:79:511:189:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ments.  We consider both continuous- or discrete-action settings.  For the continuous action
4:124:9144:17:17:79:511:172:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:case, we propose a local polynomial regression procedure.  The general trading game model
4:125:9233:17:17:79:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:imposes the restriction that equilibrium menus must be convex, and therefore we also pro-
4:126:9322:17:17:79:511:138:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:poseempirical ironingprocedures that enforce menu convexity during estimation through
4:127:9407:17:35:79:240:121:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:flexible shape-constrained splines.
4:128:9442:35:15:79:511:86:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:1Our approach can be thought of as a generalization of the first price auction approach of Guerre, Perrigne,
4:129:9550:15:0:79:479:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:and Vuong (2000) to settings where the rules of the game or equilibrium of the game are unknown.
5:130:9714:0:17:91:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We  analyze  the  performance  of  our  estimation  procedure  in  simulations  of  first  price
5:131:9810:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:auctions relative to the approach of Guerre, Perrigne, and Vuong (2000).  While our esti-
5:132:9899:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mator performs well in terms of finite-sample mean squared error, the approach of Guerre,
5:133:9988:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Perrigne, and Vuong (2000) clearly outperforms our estimator, as it exploits the knowledge
5:134:10078:17:17:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that  the  game  is  indeed  a  first  price  auction.   We  then  simulate  the  bilateral  bargaining
5:135:10181:17:16:79:511:603:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:game studied in Satterthwaite and Williams (1989) and tie our hands, treating the simu-
5:136:10268:16:17:79:511:587:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:lated data as though it came from a bargaining game with an unknown extensive form, as
5:137:10354:17:17:79:511:570:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is this case with bargaining data in many real-world settings.2We demonstrate that our
5:138:10440:17:17:79:511:553:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:method again performs well.  We emphasize that if a researcher is analyzing a game with
5:139:10527:17:17:79:511:536:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:known rules and an existing,  well-established estimation approach,  as in the case of first
5:140:10619:17:17:79:511:519:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:price auctions, existing tools should be used.  The advantage of our approach is in analyzing
5:141:10712:17:16:79:511:502:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:settings which, in spite of being quite common forms of trade—such as bargaining—do not
5:142:10799:16:21:79:442:486:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:have well-established tools or well-understood equilibrium characterizations.
5:143:10876:21:17:91:511:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:The tools we propose can be extended in a number of ways.  First, we demonstrate that
5:144:10961:17:17:79:511:448:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in certain games our identification and estimation approach can accommodate observed as
5:145:11048:17:16:79:511:431:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:well as unobserved game-level heterogeneity; that is, a component of player valuations that
5:146:11139:16:17:79:511:415:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is  common  to  all  players.   Second,  we  show  that  independence  of  agents’  values  can  be
5:147:11238:17:21:79:436:398:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:relaxed when the equilibrium is assumed to be separating in agents’ types.
5:148:11312:21:16:91:511:377:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We apply our estimation approach to data from the wholesale used-car market, a large
5:149:11396:16:17:79:511:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:market fueling the supply side of US used-car industry.  The market involves individual cars
5:150:11488:17:17:79:511:344:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sold through a game of a secret reserve price auction followed by alternating-offer bargaining
5:151:11582:17:17:79:511:327:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:between the seller and high bidder when the high bid falls short of the reserve price.  This
5:152:11674:17:17:79:511:310:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:game  has  multiple  equilibria  and  no  complete  theoretical  characterization.   In  the  data,
5:153:11773:17:17:79:511:293:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:we observe the final transaction price, an indicator for whether or not trade occurred (the
5:154:11864:17:17:79:511:276:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:allocation), and the secret reserve price of the seller.  We combine our imperfectly observable
5:155:11959:17:16:79:511:259:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:actions case with our unobserved heterogeneity correction procedure to estimate the menu
5:156:12047:16:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of expected payoffs sellers choose from.  We then estimate the mapping from reported secret
5:157:12138:17:21:79:454:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:reserve prices to sellers’ true values by evaluating the derivatives of this menu.
5:158:12220:21:16:91:511:205:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:With the estimated valuations we perform a number of counterfactual exercises.  First, we
5:159:12309:16:17:79:511:189:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:evaluate how close this real-world mechanism (the auction followed by post-auction bargain-
5:160:12400:17:17:79:511:172:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ing) lies to the first-best efficient mechanism and the second-best (information-constrained)
5:161:12493:17:17:79:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:efficient  mechanism  for  this  setting  ofN>1  buyers  and  1  seller.   We  then  evaluate  the
5:162:12591:17:41:79:511:138:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mechanism that would be optimal for the seller in this setting (an auction with a public
5:163:12679:41:15:79:511:97:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:2Fudenberg and Tirole (1991) refer to the choice of a particular extensive form as a “thorny issue” when
5:164:12783:15:11:79:511:82:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:modeling bargaining,  as the actual extensive form in many real-world negotiations is unknown to the re-
5:165:12887:11:0:79:114:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:searcher.
6:166:12913:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:reserve  price)  and  the  mechanism  that  would  be  optimal  for  the  buyer  (an  auction  fol-
6:167:13012:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:lowed  by  a  take-it-or-leave-it  offer  by  the  high  bidder  to  the  seller).   We  find  that  the
6:168:13116:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:auction-plus-bargaining mechanism used in practice only has a small efficiency loss relative
6:169:13208:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to  the  first-best  or  second-best,  and  it  outperforms  the  seller-optimal  and  buyer-optimal
6:170:13308:17:17:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mechanisms,  both  in  terms  of  total  surplus  and  the  volume  of  trade.   We  also  examine
6:171:13406:17:16:79:511:603:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:distributional implications of mechanism choice:  who gets what share of the surplus.  We
6:172:13495:16:17:79:511:587:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:find that the mechanism favors sellers, in the sense that it gives them a larger share of the
6:173:13588:17:17:79:511:570:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:surplus, but we find that it favors sellers less-so than the second-best mechanism would.  We
6:174:13681:17:17:79:511:553:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:also examine the implications of the Myerson and Satterthwaite (1983) Theorem for this
6:175:13767:17:17:79:511:536:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:setting. We find that second-best efficiency is very close to first-best efficiency in our setting,
6:176:13866:17:20:79:511:519:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:largely because competition between buyers decreases losses from asymmetric information.
6:177:13954:20:17:91:511:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We  see  the  results  presented  in  this  paper  as  having  potential  to  be  used  to  identify
6:178:14054:17:17:79:511:482:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and estimate agents’ preferences from complex games or mechanisms in a variety of set-
6:179:14140:17:17:79:511:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tings,  such  as  wage  bargaining  (Cramton  and  Tracy  1992),  pre-trial  settlement  (Silveira
6:180:14238:17:17:79:511:448:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:2017; Prescott, Spier, and Yoon 2014), bargaining in developing countries (Keniston 2011),
6:181:14328:17:16:79:511:431:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:state-run procurement mechanisms (Best, Hjort, and Szakonyi (2017)), international trade
6:182:14416:16:17:79:511:415:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:negotiations  (Bagwell,  Staiger,  and  Yurukoglu  2014),  bargaining  between  hospitals  and
6:183:14510:17:17:79:511:398:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:suppliers (Grennan and Swanson 2016), public housing allocation mechanisms (Waldinger
6:184:14595:17:54:79:165:381:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:2017), and others.
6:185:14613:54:17:79:511:327:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f5:B:Related  Literature.Our  identification  and  estimation  approach  is  related  to  existing
6:186:14706:17:16:79:511:310:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:approaches  for  specific  types  of  games,  such  as  Guerre,  Perrigne,  and  Vuong  (2000)  for
6:187:14805:16:17:79:511:294:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:first price auctions.  Similar approaches have since been applied to many other specific set-
6:188:14898:17:17:79:511:277:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tings.  For example, the ad auctions literature (Varian, 2009; Athey and Nekipelov, 2010;
6:189:14987:17:17:79:511:260:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Nekipelov, Syrgkanis, and Tardos, 2015) discusses value identification in a manner that is
6:190:15077:17:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:close  to  ours.   Related  two-step  approaches  have  also  been  applied  to  treasury  auctions
6:191:15176:17:17:79:511:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(Horta ̧csu  and  McAdams,  2010),  auctions  for  bundles  of  goods  (Gentry,  Komarova,  and
6:192:15271:17:16:79:511:209:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Schiraldi, 2014), assignment mechanisms (Agarwal and Somaini, 2018), demand curve esti-
6:193:15358:16:17:79:511:193:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mation in e-commerce (Einav, Kuchler, Levin, and Sundaresan, 2015), and general dynamic
6:194:15445:17:21:79:282:176:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:games (Bajari, Benkard, and Levin, 2007).
6:195:15486:21:16:91:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:In a related, contemporaneous study, Kline (2016) focuses on identification, but not es-
6:196:15574:16:17:79:511:139:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:timation,  in a class of games that overlaps with the class we study:  trading games with
6:197:15663:17:17:79:511:122:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:monotone equilibria and perfectly observable actions.  We see his study as complementary to
6:198:15754:17:17:79:511:105:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ours; whereas his results apply to settings with correlated values, we only discuss correlated
6:199:15848:17:17:79:511:88:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:values  briefly  in  Section  7.   Our  study  instead  focuses  primarily  on  the  case  of  indepen-
6:200:15951:17:0:79:511:71:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:dent values, deriving additional identification results regarding menu convexity, imperfectly
7:201:16112:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:observable actions, and unobserved game-level heterogeneity, and presenting estimation ap-
7:202:16202:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:proaches for each of these cases.  Our results for handling heterogeneity relate to arguments
7:203:16295:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in Krasnokutskaya (2011), which have previously been applied primarily to particular auc-
7:204:16384:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tion settings and not incomplete information trading games more broadly.  Our extension to
7:205:16474:17:20:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:correlated private values settings relates to arguments from Li, Perrigne, and Vuong (2002).
7:206:16566:20:17:91:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Our  exposition  aims  to  emphasize  several  key  points.   First,  while  our  identification
7:207:16662:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:arguments in the case ofperfectly observableare related to ideas that have been applied to
7:208:16752:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:other specific settings in the past, we illustrate here that these identification results largely
7:209:16849:17:17:79:511:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:only require taking a stance on the structure of agents’ utility functions, not the specific
7:210:16941:17:16:79:511:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:rules of the game being played.  These approaches can be applied in any kind of trading
7:211:17028:16:17:79:511:516:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:procedure with observed actions, so long as agents’ utility functions are assumed to be affine
7:212:17122:17:17:79:511:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in expected trade probabilities and transfers.  We hope that our general exposition can help
7:213:17214:17:17:79:511:482:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to conceptually unify the many independent identification results derived in specific settings
7:214:17308:17:17:79:511:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in the literature.  We also highlight that our approach in the observed actions case can apply
7:215:17402:17:17:79:511:448:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in games without unique equilibria and that are currently understudied empirically, such
7:216:17490:17:16:79:511:431:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:as  median-  or  average-price  auctions  (Cramton,  Ellermeyer,  and  Katzman  2015;  Chang,
7:217:17583:16:17:79:511:415:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Chen,  and  Salmon  2014;  Decarolis  2018)  or  double  auctions  (Chatterjee  and  Samuelson
7:218:17677:17:21:79:354:398:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:1983; Satterthwaite and Williams 1989; Li and Liu 2015).
7:219:17733:21:16:91:511:377:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Our approach to identification and estimation withimperfectly observedactions in Sec-
7:220:17818:16:17:79:511:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tion  4  is  new  and  unrelated  to  previous  approaches.   It  can  allow  the  econometrician  to
7:221:17919:17:17:79:511:344:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:avoid  modeling  a  complex  game  and  instead  use  a  partially  observed  action  vector  or  a
7:222:18018:17:17:79:511:327:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:characteristic of an agent not observed by other agents to identify payoff menus and infer
7:223:18108:17:17:79:511:310:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:underlying  valuations.   This  can  particularly  useful  in  many  complex  games  that  do  not
7:224:18206:17:17:79:511:293:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:immediately fit the mold of existing empirical frameworks and tools, such as sequential bi-
7:225:18297:17:17:79:511:276:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:lateral bargaining (Keniston 2011; Ambrus, Chaney, and Salitskiy 2018), auctions followed
7:226:18386:17:16:79:511:259:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:by bargaining (Elyakime, Laffont, Loisel, and Vuong 1997; Larsen 2014; An and Tang 2016),
7:227:18475:16:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:auctions with collusion (Asker 2010; Kawai and Nakabayashi 2015),  or other multi-stage
7:228:18562:17:21:79:238:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:games of incomplete information.
7:229:18594:21:16:91:511:205:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Furthermore, as we show in Section 3, the general trading game model imposes a simple
7:230:18679:16:17:79:511:189:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:empirical restriction, independently of the extensive-form game being played:  equilibrium
7:231:18769:17:17:79:511:172:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:menus{(Pi(ai),Ti(ai))}must  be  convex.   This  unifies  a  number  of  known  restrictions
7:232:18860:17:17:79:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:on equilibrium outcomes in specific settings:  menu convexity is exactly equivalent to the
7:233:18950:17:17:79:511:138:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:restrictions  on  first-price  auction  equilibrium  outcomes  in  Guerre,  Perrigne,  and  Vuong
7:234:19047:17:17:79:511:121:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(2000), and the condition that marginal revenues are monotone in the ad auctions (Varian,
7:235:19136:17:16:79:511:104:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:2009; Athey and Nekipelov, 2010; Nekipelov, Syrgkanis, and Tardos, 2015) and e-commerce
7:236:19223:16:0:79:511:88:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(Einav, Kuchler, Levin, and Sundaresan, 2015) literatures.  Our paper demonstrates how to
8:237:19329:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:exploit this restriction.  We propose estimation procedures in Section 5 below that enforce
8:238:19420:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:convexity  of  equilibrium  menus,  and  our  methodology  for  handling  imperfectly  observed
8:239:19515:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:actions  in  Section  4  also  relies  on  menu  convexity.   In  principle,  menu  convexity  could
8:240:19615:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:be  used  as  a  test  of  the  utility  and  equilibrium  assumptions  of  the  trading  game  model,
8:241:19717:17:60:79:316:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:independently of the particular rules of the game.
8:242:19767:60:26:270:320:560:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f6:?:2.Model

9:274:22095:28:16:79:510:577:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f5:B:Example 1.Auction:  Agents{1 . . .m}participate in an auction.  Actionsaibelong to a
9:275:22179:16:17:79:511:561:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:space that depends on the rules of the auction.  For example, in a sealed-bid auction, the
9:276:22269:17:17:79:511:544:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:actions are sealed bids inR.  In an ascending or multi-round auction, actions are history-
9:277:22359:17:17:79:511:527:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:contingent bidding strategies.  Agents’ outside options are to leave without participating in
9:278:22452:17:27:79:222:510:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the auction, leading to ̄xi=0.
9:279:22482:27:17:79:511:483:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f5:B:Example 2.Bargaining:  A seller (player 1) and a buyer (player 2) bargain over an indi-
9:280:22569:17:17:79:510:466:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:visible good.  The seller’s outside option is ̄x1=1, and the buyer’s outside option is ̄x2=0.

10:329:24196:20:17:91:510:634:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Equation (3) is a necessary and sufficient condition for strategiessi(vi)to constitute a

10:335:24732:17:16:79:511:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:indexed by action choicesai.  This menu is a sufficient statistic fori’s choice in equilibrium:
10:336:24827:16:17:79:511:516:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:given her typevi, each agentichooses the item(Pi(ai),Ti(ai))from the equilibrium menu
10:337:24912:17:17:79:511:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that affords her the highest utility.  The equilibrium menu is also sufficient for characterizing
10:338:25009:17:17:79:511:482:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:agents’ welfare gains from participating in trade; the expected welfare gain of typeviis the
10:339:25101:17:20:79:191:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:maximized value of (2).
10:340:25124:20:17:91:511:445:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:In what follows, we will assume that the econometrician observes data from many inde-
10:341:25209:17:17:79:511:428:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:pendent realizations of the same underlying trading game.  As mentioned above,  we will
10:342:25296:17:17:79:511:411:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:further assume that all realizations of the game represent play from the same Bayes-Nash
10:343:25384:17:17:79:511:394:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Equilibrium.  While this assumption is common in the structural empirical literature, it is
10:344:25475:17:16:79:511:377:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:certainly strong.  We emphasize here, however, that this assumption does not imply that
10:345:25562:16:17:79:511:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the underlying game need only have a single equilibrium, only that the data represents play
10:346:25653:17:17:79:511:344:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:from a single equilibrium.  This therefore allows the data to speak as to the equilibrium
10:347:25742:17:17:79:511:327:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:selection from a (potentially infinite) set of equilibria rather than requiring the researcher to
10:348:25839:17:17:79:511:310:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:impose an equilibrium refinement.  This is particularly useful in the settings we seek to ana-
10:349:25933:17:17:79:511:293:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:lyze, as many of these are cases with multiple equilibria that are qualitatively very different
10:350:26028:17:17:79:510:276:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f4:B:and where theoretical equilibrium refinements do not always yield a unique equilibrium.3
10:351:26116:17:16:79:511:259:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Moreover, all of our results in this paper still hold if the assumption of a single equilibrium
10:352:26211:16:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in  the  data  is  relaxed  to  instead  assume  that,  if  the  equilibrium  does  indeed  differ  from
10:353:26315:17:17:79:511:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:one realization of the game to another, then which equilibrium is selected depends only on
10:354:26405:17:17:79:511:209:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:features in the data that are observable to the econometrician and can thus be controlled
10:355:26494:17:20:79:281:192:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:for.  We discuss this further in Section 9.4.
10:356:26539:20:17:91:511:172:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:By allowing all value distributionsFiand action setsAito be distinct, we allow agents
10:357:26624:17:17:79:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to be completely asymmetric.  This is important for games in which players play different
10:358:26713:17:17:79:511:138:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:roles,  such as in bilateral bargaining settings,  as in Example 2.  In some cases below,  we
10:359:26806:17:24:79:511:121:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:will  use  the  subscriptsito  denote  a  particular  role  played  by  the  agent,  such  as  using
10:360:26906:24:15:79:511:97:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:3For  example,  in  the  case  of  bilateral  bargaining,  proposed  equilibrium  refinements  often  fail  to  exist  or
10:361:27027:15:11:79:511:82:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:result in equilibria that predict immediate agreement.  See discussion in Ausubel, Cramton, and Deneckere
10:362:27132:11:0:79:212:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:(2002) or results in Perry (1986).
11:363:27234:0:17:79:510:688:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:i∈{S,B}indexing whether the player is a seller or buyer in bargaining.  In practice, each
11:364:27323:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:instance of the trading game may involve classes of agents who are indistinguishable.  For
11:365:27413:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:example,  different bidders in an auction may be indistinguishable to the econometrician,
11:366:27502:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:or only distinguishable based on certain observables; an example is the case of loggers vs.
11:367:27593:17:17:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mills  bidding  in  timber  auctions  (Athey,  Coey,  and  Levin  2013).   In  such  settings,  the
11:368:27692:17:16:79:511:603:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:econometrician may wish to model all players from a certain class as drawing valuations
11:369:27779:16:17:79:511:587:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:from a single distribution.  All of our identification and estimation results can be thought
11:370:27871:17:64:79:250:570:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of as applying to such cases as well.
11:371:27908:64:27:164:426:506:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f6:?:3.Identification with Fully Observed Actions
11:372:27952:27:17:91:511:479:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:In this section, we derive identification results for the model described above, assuming
11:373:28041:17:17:79:511:462:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that the econometrician fully observes agents’ actions from many instances of equilibrium
11:374:28130:17:17:79:511:445:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:play of the trading gameG. We first analyze the case where the equilibrium is not necessarily
11:375:28223:17:16:79:511:428:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:increasing or in pure strategies.  We then demonstrate stronger results that can be obtained
11:376:28315:16:17:79:511:412:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:when such an increasing, pure-strategy equilibrium does exist.  In each instance of the game,
11:377:28408:17:17:79:510:395:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:valuesVi, for each agenti∈{1, ...,m}, are independently drawn fromFi(and these actions
11:378:28494:17:17:79:511:378:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:are independent across instances of the game).  Agents then take actions corresponding to
11:379:28583:17:17:79:511:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a set of equilibrium strategies(s1(·), . . . ,sm(·)).  We assume in this section that in each
11:380:28676:17:17:79:510:344:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:instance of the game, the econometrician observesxi(the allocation for agenti),ti(the
11:381:28761:17:20:79:292:327:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:transfer for agenti), and agenti’s actionai.
11:382:28805:20:17:91:511:307:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Examples  of  cases  in  which  the  econometrician  might  observe  agents’  actions  are  any
11:383:28900:17:17:79:511:290:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sealed-bid trading game or any simultaneous-move trading game.  This includes not only
11:384:28986:17:17:79:511:273:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:first-price or second price auctions, where the structure of equilibria is well-known in the
11:385:29078:17:16:79:511:256:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:theoretical and empirical literature, but also any arbitrary sealed-bid trading game where
11:386:29168:16:17:79:511:240:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:such properties may be less well-known or strategies less well-behaved, such as the median-
11:387:29259:17:17:79:511:223:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:price auction used in Medicare durable good equipment auctions, which is known to poten-
11:388:29347:17:17:79:511:206:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tially yield equilibria that are non-increasing (Cramton, Ellermeyer, and Katzman 2015); or
11:389:29438:17:17:79:511:189:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sealed-bid bilateral bargaining games, such as thekdouble auction, which are known to have
11:390:29528:17:17:79:511:172:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:multiple,  qualitatively different equilibria (Chatterjee and Samuelson 1983; Satterthwaite
11:391:29619:17:16:79:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and Williams 1989; Li and Liu 2015).  Another example is the average-bid auction, which
11:392:29706:16:17:79:511:139:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Chang, Chen, and Salmon (2014) and Decarolis (2018) demonstrate can have multiple equi-
11:393:29793:17:17:79:511:122:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:libria and, in some cases, no equilibria in increasing strategies.  Decarolis (2018) highlights
11:394:29888:17:17:79:511:105:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that this mechanism is used for public procurement by state agencies in Florida and New
11:395:29975:17:17:79:511:88:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:York, as well as in Chile, China, Colombia, Italy, Japan, Peru, Malaysia, Switzerland, and
11:396:30065:17:0:79:117:71:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Taiwan.
12:397:30090:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:3.1.Fully Observed Actions: General Case.In Section 2, we argued that the expected

12:400:30351:17:17:79:510:637:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f15:B:These expected outcome functions are simply conditional expectations of outcomesxi,ti

13:559:34027:16:17:79:511:294:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:design that implementable allocation rules must be monotone, assigning higher bundles to
13:560:34115:17:17:79:511:277:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:higher  types.   Intuitively,  under  our  “convex  menu”  interpretation  of  equilibria,  convex

13:562:34303:17:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:additional probability.  Agents who choose bundles with higherPi(ai)pay higher average
13:563:34389:17:20:79:368:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:costs per unit probability, and thus must have higher values.

15:640:38111:44:27:146:444:416:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f6:?:4.Identification with Imperfectly Observed Actions
15:641:38161:27:17:91:511:389:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:In  many  contexts,  it  is  impossible  for  the  econometrician  to  observe  all  elements  of  a
15:642:38261:17:17:79:511:372:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:realization of the actionai.  For example,  in a multiple-offer bargaining game,  observing
15:643:38352:17:16:79:511:355:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f10:F:aiwould entail observing a vector of all ofi’s actionscontingent on all possible sequences
15:644:38442:16:17:79:511:339:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of  offers  from  other  agents,  or  in  an  ascending  auction,  all  ofi’s  bid  strategies  over  all
15:645:38547:17:17:79:511:322:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sequences of opponent bids, within a single instance of the game.  Thus, observingaiwould
15:646:38636:17:17:79:511:305:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:not simply mean observing what actionsitook, but what actionsiwould have takenin every
15:647:38722:17:17:79:511:288:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:history of the game, including those not reached; this would be equivalent to observing a
15:648:38811:17:20:79:505:271:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:set of instructions playeriwould have given to a third-party agent to play on her behalf.
15:649:38900:20:17:91:511:251:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:However,  in  many  of  these  cases  where  the  action  is  a  multidimensional  vector,  the
15:650:38995:17:17:79:511:234:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:econometrician  will  be  able  to  observe  some  portion  of  an  agent’s  action  vector  or  will
15:651:39096:17:17:79:511:217:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:be  able  to  observe  some  other  feature  in  the  dataset  that  is  correlated  with  an  agent’s
15:652:39198:17:17:79:511:200:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:unobserved action vector.  We refer to such an object—either a partially observed action
15:653:39286:17:16:79:511:183:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:or a separate feature in the dataset correlated with an agent’s action—as anaction shifter,

17:709:43631:28:17:91:511:378:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:The equality on the second line follows by the law of iterated expectations and the equality
17:710:43723:17:17:79:511:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:on third line follows by the fact thatZiis independent ofA−i, so the inner conditioning on

17:712:43900:17:17:79:511:327:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:outcomes defining the menu.  The above argument shows that conditional expectations of
17:713:43986:17:16:79:511:310:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:xi,tiwith respect tozirecover convex combinations of(Pi(ai),Ti(ai))pairs.  Since the

17:715:44164:17:17:79:511:277:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of{(Pi(ai),Ti(ai))}.   In  other  words,  for  anyzithat  satisfies  Definition  1,  the  graph

17:717:44351:17:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:obtain a lower bound on the utility of any given typeviin equilibrium, or, equivalently, an

23:1200:57929:19:17:79:511:342:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:observed action,aj, and taking the coefficient on the linear term in (12),ˆβ1.  Similarly, an
23:1201:58022:17:17:79:511:325:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimate of the first derivativeˆP′(a)is given by running a local polynomial regression of
23:1202:58112:17:17:79:511:308:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the observed allocation,xj(i.e., an indicator for whether the player won), on the observed
23:1203:58202:17:20:79:432:291:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f4:B:action,aj, and taking the coefficient on the linear term in the regression.6
23:1204:58278:20:17:91:510:271:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f14:A:As in Section 5.1, this estimation procedure may result in a nonconvex{(P(a),T(a))}
23:1205:58361:17:62:79:511:254:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:menu,  and it may be desirable to “iron” the empirical menu function,  constraining it to
23:1206:58450:62:17:79:511:192:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:6For the bandwidth, Fan and Gijbels, Chapter 4.2, describes the following rule-of-thumb selection procedure:
23:1207:58558:17:11:79:511:175:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:First, one fits a global quintic polynomial by standard ordinary least squares,ˆˆT(a)=α0+α1a. . .+α5a5.
23:1208:58661:11:11:79:511:164:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:Let  the  residual  variance  from  the  regression  be ̃σ2.   The  rule-of-thumb  bandwidth  is  then  equal  to  the
23:1209:58779:11:29:79:264:153:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:following “variance components”-like formula:
23:1210:58824:29:0:226:275:124:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f8:A:ˆh=Cν,p(K)
23:1211:58834:0:16:277:283:143:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f21:?:
23:1212:58835:16:10:277:320:127:9:g_d0_f21:6:g_d0_f25:?: ̃σ2
23:1213:58841:10:9:284:299:117:9:g_d0_f22:6:g_d0_f15:?:∑n
23:1214:58843:9:0:294:306:108:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f25:?:i=1
23:1215:58846:0:7:307:318:120:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f11:?:(ˆ
23:1216:58848:7:0:313:336:113:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f8:?:ˆT′′(a)
23:1217:58855:0:0:336:346:120:9:g_d0_f21:6:g_d0_f25:A:)2
23:1218:58857:0:16:347:353:143:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f21:?:
23:1219:58858:16:0:347:353:127:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f21:?:
23:1220:58860:0:21:354:357:143:5:g_d0_f26:5:g_d0_f26:A:17
23:1221:58862:21:29:361:510:122:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:,(13)
23:1222:58867:29:11:79:511:93:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:whereCν,p(K)is a kernel-specific constant.  Fan and Gijbels, Table 3.2, reports this constant as approxi-
23:1223:58972:11:11:79:511:82:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:mately 0.884 for the Gaussian kernel, 2.275 for the Epanechnikov kernel, and 2.869 for the triweight kernel.
23:1224:59080:11:0:79:476:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:This procedure chooses smaller bandwidths for functions that can be fitted better by polynomials.
24:1225:59195:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:be convex during estimation.7In addition, it may be desirable in some contexts to enforce
24:1226:59284:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:monotonicity  of  theP(a)function.   In  a  manner  similar  to  Judd  (1998)  and  Schumaker
24:1227:59377:17:17:79:510:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f8:B:(1983), we propose a spline-based procedure to nonparametrically estimate theP(·),T(·)
24:1228:59463:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:functions while imposing convexity of the{(P(a),T(a))}menu.  In Appendix B, we describe
24:1229:59550:17:17:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the construction of the quadratic and cubic spline bases in detail.  Our estimation approach
24:1230:59642:17:16:79:511:603:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:proceeds in two stages:  first,P(a)is nonparametrically estimated as a smooth function of
24:1231:59731:16:17:79:510:587:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:a, possibly constrained to be monotonic, using quadratic splines.  Then,T(·)is estimated
24:1232:59819:17:17:79:510:570:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:as the composite functionˆT(P(a)), whereˆT(·)is constrained to be a convex cubic spline.
24:1233:59907:17:17:79:511:553:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Constraining  the  quadratic  (cubic)  spline  coefficients  to  be  nonnegative  ensures  that  the
24:1234:60007:17:17:79:511:536:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:target function is nondecreasing (convex).  Note that, by construction, the quadratic splines
24:1235:60100:17:14:79:511:519:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:have two continuous derivatives, and the cubic splines three continuous derivatives.  Since
24:1236:60191:14:19:79:511:505:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ˆT(p)is a cubic spline, the estimated mappings−1(a)=dTdPis guaranteed to be continuous
24:1237:60277:19:30:79:165:486:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and differentiable.
24:1238:60296:30:27:216:374:456:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f6:A:6.Monte Carlo Simulations
24:1239:60321:27:17:79:511:429:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:6.1.First-Price  Auction  Simulations.In  this  section,  we  simulate  data  from  a  first-
24:1240:60414:17:17:79:511:412:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:price auction and estimate values using the standard Guerre, Perrigne, and Vuong (2000)
24:1241:60501:17:16:79:511:395:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(GPV) approach as well as our approaches based on local polynomial regressions and convex
24:1242:60590:16:17:79:510:379:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:splines.  We usem=5 bidders for each auction instance, using uniform, exponential and
24:1243:60675:17:17:79:511:362:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:lognormal value distributions.  We generate datasets of size 4,000, 16,000, and 40,000 for
24:1244:60765:17:17:79:511:345:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimation; we solve for the unique equilibrium as in GPV, and then simulate and estimate
24:1245:60854:17:20:79:392:328:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:from each combination of distribution and dataset size 200 times.
24:1246:60919:20:28:91:262:308:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:The GPV estimator can be written:
24:1247:60952:28:0:251:305:280:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f8:?:ˆv(a)=a+
24:1248:60960:0:18:310:334:291:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f8:?:ˆ ̄G(a)
24:1249:60967:18:0:310:333:273:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f8:?:ˆ ̄g(a)
24:1250:60974:0:32:335:338:280:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:,
24:1251:60975:32:16:79:511:248:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:wherevis  the  agent’s  value,ais  the  agent’s  bid,  andˆ ̄G(·),ˆ ̄g(·)are  estimates  of  the
24:1252:61071:16:17:79:510:232:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:distribution and density functions of themaximum opposing bid, rather than the distribution
24:1253:61162:17:17:79:511:215:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of all bids.8We estimateˆ ̄g(·)using a kernel density estimator, using Gaussian kernels with
24:1254:61254:17:17:79:511:198:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:bandwidth  chosen  using  the  Silverman  (1986)  rule  of  thumb.   We  estimateˆ ̄G(·)using  a
24:1255:61350:17:18:79:511:181:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:linearly interpolated empirical CDF. To implement our local polynomial regression method,
24:1256:61439:18:14:79:511:163:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:7Menu convexity corresponds exactly to monotonicity of Myerson (1981) marginal revenue, hence “ironing”
24:1257:61542:14:11:79:511:149:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:in this context is exactly equivalent to the Myersonian procedure of enforcing marginal revenue monotonicity
24:1258:61650:11:9:79:160:138:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:for a demand curve.
24:1259:61669:9:14:79:511:129:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:8While we draw i.i.d.  bids for simulation, we estimate values allowing for bidders to be potentially drawn
24:1260:61776:14:11:79:511:115:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:from different distributions.  The symmetric GPV estimator uses multiple data points from each auction,
24:1261:61879:11:11:79:511:104:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:and could technically be implemented with only observing one auction (with many bidders) whereas our
24:1262:61979:11:11:79:511:93:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:approach requires observing multiple instances of the game.  We use the asymmetric version here to hold
24:1263:62082:11:11:79:511:82:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:fixed the effective sample size between our procedure and GPV, comparing only the estimation procedures’
24:1264:62186:11:0:79:135:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:performances.
25:1265:62268:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:we run local quadratic regressions to estimate derivatives as described in Section 5.2, using
25:1266:62361:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Gaussian  kernels  with  bandwidths  equal  to  half9the  Fan-Gijbels  rule  of  thumb  in  (13).
25:1267:62458:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:To implement our convex spline method, we first estimatePi(·)separately for each agent
25:1268:62544:17:17:79:510:637:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:iusing  a  local  linear  regression,  with  bandwidth  chosen  using  a  rule  of  thumb  that  Fan
25:1269:62644:17:17:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and Gijbels propose for local linear regression.  Then, we estimate the functionTi(Pi)for
25:1270:62733:17:16:79:510:603:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:each agentiusing convex splines with 10 knots uniformly separated in bid quantile space,
25:1271:62821:16:17:79:511:587:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:minimizing the sum of squared errors from the(a,x,t)triples observed in data.  We did not
25:1272:62910:17:17:79:511:570:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:explicitly apply any procedure for spline knot selection, but we found that results were not
25:1273:63002:17:21:79:334:553:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:very sensitive to using knot counts between 5 and 20.
25:1274:63055:21:16:91:511:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We show pointwise 95% coverage bands from 200 estimation sample for both estimators,
25:1275:63139:16:17:79:511:516:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:for the case of the exponential distribution withN=4, 000 in Figure 3.  In Table 1,  for
25:1276:63227:17:17:79:511:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:all  specifications  we  used,  we  show  average  mean  squared  errors  normalized  by  the  true
25:1277:63326:17:20:79:442:482:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f4:B:variance in values, for bid values between the 20th and 80th bid quantiles.10
25:1278:63403:20:17:91:511:462:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We find that GPV significantly outperforms both of our estimators:  the mean squared
25:1279:63487:17:17:79:511:445:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:error  of  GPV  is  less  than  1  percent  in  all  of  the  simulation  specifications,  and  in  some
25:1280:63591:17:17:79:511:428:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:cases it is even below 0.1%.  In absolute terms, however, both the local quadratic and spline
25:1281:63684:17:17:79:511:411:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimators perform fairly well, achieving below 10% MSE in all specifications, and achieving
25:1282:63776:17:20:79:361:394:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:around 1% MSE in specifications with 40,000 observations.
25:1283:63833:20:17:91:511:374:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Our proposed spline estimator may have a number of qualitative benefits over the local
25:1284:63919:17:17:79:511:357:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:quadratic regression estimator. First, it is guaranteed to produce convex menus for any given
25:1285:64012:17:17:79:511:340:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimation instance,  which may be desirable in settings where value and menu estimates
25:1286:64099:17:17:79:511:323:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:are  used  for  economic  counterfactuals.   Second,  as  we  demonstrate  in  Section  7.2,  the
25:1287:64196:17:16:79:511:306:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:spline estimator allows the researcher to incorporate an unobserved heterogeneity correction
25:1288:64288:16:17:79:511:290:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:procedure.  If unobserved heterogeneity is not a serious issue,  we suggest using the local
25:1289:64379:17:17:79:511:273:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:quadratic regression estimator, as its finite-sample performance appears to exceed that of the
25:1290:64473:17:17:79:511:256:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:spline estimator.  In cases where unobserved heterogeneity or other multi-step procedures
25:1291:64562:17:17:79:511:239:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that benefit from parametric estimation are needed, or in cases where data is sparse and
25:1292:64650:17:17:79:511:222:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:enforcing menu convexity is important for statistical reasons, our spline procedure may be
25:1293:64740:17:16:79:511:205:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:preferable despite its worse finite-sample performance.  We use the splines approach in our
25:1294:64831:16:35:79:273:189:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:empirical application in Section 8 below.
25:1295:64872:35:14:79:511:154:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:9This  is  an  ad-hoc  adjustment,  because  we  found  that  the  estimator  performed  somewhat  better  with
25:1296:64983:14:11:79:511:140:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:smaller bandwidths, possibly because this reduces bias in the estimator when the target function is relatively
25:1297:65093:11:9:79:126:129:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:nonsmooth.
25:1298:65103:9:14:79:511:120:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:10While this is a large truncation, as Figure 3 shows, both GPV and our local quadratic regression estimator
25:1299:65211:14:12:79:511:106:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:can function very poorly towards the lower end of the support of the bid distribution.  For our estimator,
25:1300:65317:12:12:79:510:94:9:g_d0_f11:6:g_d0_f17:F:this is essentially because the probability of winning and transfer both become very small; the ratioT′(b)P′(b)
25:1301:65428:12:11:79:511:82:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:thus becomes numerically unstable.  Thus MSE comparisons are more meaningful for bids well inside the
25:1302:65529:11:0:79:264:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:interior of the support of the bid distribution.
26:1303:65595:0:17:91:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We interpret these first-price auction simulation results as suggesting that if the researcher
26:1304:65689:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is well aware that the game generating the data is indeed a first-price auction, the researcher
26:1305:65784:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:should use the standard GPV approach for identification and estimation.  If, however, the
26:1306:65873:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:researcher has data by some unknown bidding procedure or by some unknown equilibrium
26:1307:65957:17:17:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:selection  rule,  or  from  a  bidding  procedure  for  which  no  specific,  standard  tool  has  yet
26:1308:66059:17:16:79:511:603:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:been derived, and wishes to identify and estimate valuations in a manner that is robust to
26:1309:66149:16:58:79:480:587:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:misspecification of these features of the game, our menu approach can perform well.
26:1310:66232:58:16:79:511:529:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:6.2.Bargaining Simulations.To further illustrate our method, we choose a setting for
26:1311:66316:16:17:79:511:513:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:which, unlike first-price auctions, there is no existing off-the-shelf method for estimation:
26:1312:66409:17:17:79:511:496:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a  bargaining  game  with  two-sided  incomplete  information.   The  theoretical  literature  on
26:1313:66506:17:17:79:511:479:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:incomplete information bargaining demonstrates that such games in general have multiple
26:1314:66593:17:17:79:511:462:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:equilibria that are difficult to characterize.  Here, we generate data from a particular equilib-
26:1315:66690:17:17:79:511:445:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:rium from such a game.  In order to do so, we adopt the bilateral bargaining game described
26:1316:66781:17:16:79:511:428:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:B:in Satterthwaite and Williams (1989).  Players’ roles are denotedi∈{B,S}.  The buyerB
26:1317:66866:16:17:79:511:412:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and sellerShave private valuations and make offers.  If the buyer’s offer (aB) exceeds that
26:1318:66957:17:17:79:511:395:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of the seller (aS), trade occurs at pricet=kaS+(1−k)aB, wherek∈[0, 1].  The parameter
26:1319:67042:17:17:79:511:378:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:kcan be considered a bargaining power weight.  A game withk=1 corresponds to the
26:1320:67122:17:17:79:510:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:seller-optimal mechanism (a take-it-or-leave-it offer by the seller) and a game withk=0
26:1321:67209:17:17:79:511:344:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:corresponds to the buyer-optimal mechanism (a take-it-or-leave-it offer by the buyer).  This
26:1322:67301:17:17:79:510:327:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:game is referred to in the literature as akdouble auction (see also Chatterjee and Samuel-
26:1323:67391:17:16:79:511:310:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:son 1983).  Satterthwaite and Williams (1989) demonstrate that a continuum of equilibria
26:1324:67479:16:17:79:511:294:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:exist in this game, and they provide methods to solve for a class of equilibria.  We simulate
26:1325:67572:17:21:79:403:277:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:data following their solution approach, as described in Appendix C.
26:1326:67639:21:16:91:511:256:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:A:An  observation  in  the  data  we  generate  consists  of  a  final  transfert,  an  allocationx
26:1327:67736:16:17:79:511:240:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(i.e.  an indicator for whether or not the good sold),  and a seller’s offeraS.  In applying
26:1328:67828:17:17:79:511:223:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:our estimation approach, we then deliberately tie our hands by treating the buyer’s offer
26:1329:67917:17:17:79:511:206:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and the bargaining power parameter as unknown and treating the seller’s action as though
26:1330:68005:17:17:79:511:189:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:arising from an unknown extensive form bargaining game generating the data.  Specifically,
26:1331:68095:17:17:79:511:172:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:we treat the seller’s offer as a partially observed action vector that is one-to-one with the
26:1332:68188:17:16:79:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:seller’s value as described in Section 4.  This simulated data mimmicks a type of dataset
26:1333:68277:16:17:79:511:139:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that a researcher may commonly find:  prices arising from an unknown negotiation process
26:1334:68365:17:17:79:511:122:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(i.e.  the precise extensive form of the game is unknown to the researcher).  For example,
26:1335:68455:17:17:79:511:105:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a researcher might observe housing data with transacted prices,  a measure of how many
26:1336:68541:17:17:79:511:88:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:buyers  placed  offers  on  the  house  and  failed  to  win  it,  and  the  seller’s  initial  list  price
26:1337:68648:17:0:79:329:71:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(analogous to the seller offer generated in our data).
27:1338:68771:0:17:91:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We apply our estimators to cases were valuations are distributed according to a uniform or
27:1339:68861:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:truncated Normal distribution, and for sample sizes of 4,000, 16,000, or 40,000 observations.
27:1340:68954:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:The distributional parameters for the true distributions are discussed in Appendix C. Figure
27:1341:69046:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:4  display  sellers’  offers  on  the  horizontal  axis  and  the  estimated  and  true  valuations  of
27:1342:69149:17:17:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sellers on the vertical axis for the uniformly distributed case with 4,000 observations.  The
27:1343:69242:17:16:79:511:603:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimation  procedure  performs  well  in  recovering  valuations  close  to  the  truth.   Table  2
27:1344:69342:16:17:79:511:587:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:displays  the  mean  squared  error  for  the  different  specifications,  normalized  by  the  true
27:1345:69442:17:17:79:511:570:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:variance as in Table 1.  The mean squared error of the local quadratic regression estimator
27:1346:69533:17:17:79:511:553:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is at most 10% in small samples and in larger samples it is below 5%.  The convex spline
27:1347:69621:17:20:79:511:536:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimator is less accurate in small samples, but also has MSE below 10% in larger samples.
27:1348:69711:20:17:91:511:516:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We also remark here that this estimation exercise did not exploit any information about
27:1349:69798:17:17:79:511:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the  value  ofk(the  bargaining  power),  any  offer  made  by  the  buyer,  or  the  particular
27:1350:69894:17:17:79:511:482:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium being played.  Recall that a continuum of equilibria exist to this game at any
27:1351:69984:17:17:79:511:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:value ofk.  The generated data in our simulation exercise could have come from any fixed
27:1352:70072:17:17:79:511:448:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:value  ofkand  any  fixed  equilibrium,  or  even  a  sequential  bargaining  game  completely
27:1353:70166:17:16:79:511:431:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:distinct from the statickdouble auction, and the two-step approach proposed herein would
27:1354:70254:16:17:79:511:415:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:still have returned reasonable estimates of valuations based solely on the observed first seller
27:1355:70350:17:40:79:266:398:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f4:B:offer, the allocation, and the transfer.11
27:1356:70392:40:27:143:446:358:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f6:?:7.Extensions:  Heterogeneity and Correlated Values
27:1357:70442:27:16:91:511:331:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We now provide extensions to our identification arguments provided above to settings of
27:1358:70529:16:34:79:503:315:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:game-level heterogeneity (observed and unobserved heterogeneity) and correlated values.
27:1359:70616:34:17:79:511:281:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:7.1.Observable Game-Level Heterogeneity.If realizations of the game differ in a way
27:1360:70699:17:17:79:511:264:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that is observable observable to the econometrician, such heterogeneity can easily be con-
27:1361:70789:17:17:79:511:247:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:trolled for.  In particular, the estimation procedures described in Section 5 can be extended
27:1362:70882:17:17:79:511:230:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to include a vectorYof observable characteristics (that may vary in each realization of the
27:1363:70973:17:17:79:511:213:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:game) as a control in the estimation of thePi(·)andTi(·)functions determining the menu.
27:1364:71060:17:16:79:511:196:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:If such heterogeneity enters players’ valuations and actions in an additively or multiplica-
27:1365:71152:16:17:79:511:180:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tively  separable,  single-index  form,  the econometrican can simply  regress  observations  of
27:1366:71248:17:17:79:510:163:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:actions on observations of the vectorYand treat the residuals from this regression as coming
27:1367:71340:17:17:79:511:146:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:from a “homogenized” game, as in the auction setting of Haile, Hong, and Shum (2003).
27:1368:71425:17:17:79:511:129:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:We  discuss  this  separability  condition  in  more  detail  below  when  we  discuss  unobserved
27:1369:71523:17:26:79:145:112:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:heterogeneity.
27:1370:71537:26:15:79:511:86:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:11Li and Liu (2015) propose an estimation approach for settings where the researcher instead knows that
27:1371:71640:15:0:79:257:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:the data is generated by akdouble auction.
28:1372:71700:0:17:91:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Allowing for the equilibrium menu to vary with observable heterogeneity at the game level
28:1373:71789:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:also allows for the data to represent play from different equilibria of the underlying game:
28:1374:71881:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:as long as the equilibrium selection can be controlled for using observables, the presence of
28:1375:71974:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:multiple equilibria poses no threat to identification or estimation.  We discuss this further
28:1376:72067:17:28:79:178:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in Section 9.4 below.
28:1377:72088:28:17:79:511:592:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:7.2.Unobserved Heterogeneity.We focus here on correlation induced in values through
28:1378:72171:17:17:79:511:575:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:game-level  heterogeneity  that  is  observed  by  the  players  but  not  by  the  econometrician,
28:1379:72270:17:16:79:511:558:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:similar to the unobserved auction-level heterogeneity in Krasnokutskaya (2011).  We study
28:1380:72359:16:17:79:511:542:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a class of games that we callseparable heterogeneity games, which are defined as follows.  In
28:1381:72452:17:17:79:511:525:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the first stage, common componentWis drawn from the bounded distributionFW(·)and
28:1382:72532:17:17:79:511:508:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:commonly observed by all agentsi∈{1 . . .m}but not the econometrician.  In the second
28:1383:72617:17:17:79:511:491:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:stage, agents’ private valuesViare drawn independently from distributionsFi(·); agents’
28:1384:72704:17:14:79:151:474:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:values are then
28:1385:72719:14:23:264:327:460:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:?: ̃Vi=Vi+W.
28:1386:72729:23:17:79:510:437:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:In the third stage, agents take actions ̃ai∈[ai, ̄ai], which are observed by the econometri-
28:1387:72821:17:26:79:365:420:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:cian.  We require the game to satisfy the following property:
28:1388:72882:26:17:79:510:394:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f5:B:Definition 2.We say that gameGsatisfies theseparable  heterogeneity  game  propertyif
28:1389:72967:17:24:79:231:377:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:B:for all ̃a1. . . ̃am,∆, and for alli
28:1390:73003:24:25:170:510:353:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f5:A:xi( ̃a1+∆, ̃a2+∆, . . . ̃am+∆)=xi( ̃a1, ̃a2, . . . ̃am),(14)
28:1391:73063:25:29:93:510:328:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f5:A:ti( ̃a1+∆, ̃a2+∆, . . . ̃am+∆)=ti( ̃a1, ̃a2, . . . ̃am)+∆(xi( ̃a1, ̃a2, . . . ̃am)− ̄xi).(15)
28:1392:73156:29:17:91:511:299:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:The  separable  heterogeneity  game  property  can  also  be  defined  multiplicatively.   We
28:1393:73249:17:17:79:511:282:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:focus on the additive case here for brevity.  This property implies that, if all agents increase
28:1394:73345:17:16:79:510:265:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:bids  by  a  constant  amount∆,  the  probability  of  any  agent  winning  is  unchanged,  and
28:1395:73440:16:17:79:511:249:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the prices paid by agents change by the same amount by which bids change.  Intuitively,
28:1396:73527:17:17:79:511:232:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:this property is appropriate for games which are position-invariant, in the sense that the
28:1397:73617:17:17:79:511:215:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:structure  of  the  game  is  unchanged  when  all  bids  are  changed  by  a  given  amount.   The
28:1398:73716:17:17:79:511:198:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:separable heterogeneity game property may not be appropriate, for example, in bargaining
28:1399:73804:17:17:79:511:181:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:settings  with  fixed  costs,  in  which  case  the  structure  of  the  game  may  be  qualitatively
28:1400:73905:17:20:79:429:164:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f4:B:different depending on the size of the payoff agents are bargaining over.12
28:1401:73980:20:17:91:511:144:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Since the common componentWis observed by all agents prior to agents’ action choices,
28:1402:74065:17:19:79:511:127:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:agents can condition their strategies on the common componentW; thus, we can think of
28:1403:74150:19:15:79:511:108:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:12In such settings,  one possible approach is to divide instances of the game into coarse partitions by ob-
28:1404:74257:15:11:79:511:93:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:servable characteristics that may affect payoff size.  The separable heterogeneity game property may be a
28:1405:74362:11:11:79:511:82:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:reasonable assumption within each partition, and the approach described in this section could be applied
28:1406:74466:11:0:79:149:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:within partitions.
29:1407:74553:0:17:79:510:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:agents’ strategies in separable heterogeneity games as functionssi(vi,w)mapping common

32:1607:82105:17:17:79:511:393:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is separating:  equilibrium strategies are described by thesi(vi), where eachsiis invertible.
32:1608:82198:17:17:79:511:376:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:We  show  that,  as  in  Section  3,  we  can  derive  bounds  on  the  inverse  functionsvi(·)for

32:1610:82392:17:16:79:511:342:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Kline  (2016),  which  derives  stronger  identification  results  than  ours  under  an  additional
32:1611:82492:16:21:79:290:326:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:assumption about equilibrium monotonicity.
