34:1775:86358:52:27:141:449:535:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f6:A:8.Application to Auction with Sequential Bargaining
34:1776:86409:27:17:91:511:508:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We apply our approach to study a complex game used in wholesale used-car markets,
34:1777:86490:17:16:79:511:491:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that of a secret reserve price auction followed by alternating-offer bargaining between the
34:1778:86581:16:17:79:511:475:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:seller  and  high  bidder.14The  presence  of  sequential  bargaining  in  this  mechanism,  with
34:1779:86678:17:17:79:511:458:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:both parties having private information about their valuations, puts this game in a class
34:1780:86767:17:17:79:511:441:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:for which there is no known analytical solution or full equilibrium characterization:  that
34:1781:86858:17:17:79:511:424:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of  two-sided  bargaining  games  with  two-sided  incomplete  information  and  continuum  of
34:1782:86952:17:17:79:511:407:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:agent values.  The properties of such games are unknown.  In particular, it is unknown how
34:1783:87042:17:16:79:511:390:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:efficient such a mechanism is in practice relative to efficient bargaining, and how the gains
34:1784:87135:16:17:79:511:374:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:from trade created by the mechanism are divided among the participants.15Our approach
34:1785:87220:17:17:79:511:357:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:allows us to estimate players’ valuations and expected gains from trade in this game without
34:1786:87312:17:17:79:511:340:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:imposing a particular extensive form or equilibrium selection.  We then use these objects
34:1787:87401:17:17:79:511:323:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to measure how efficient the market is and how the total welfare is split among buyers and
34:1788:87491:17:20:79:111:306:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sellers.
34:1789:87499:20:17:91:511:286:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We also use our estimates to address an additional question of interest for market design.
34:1790:87589:17:17:79:511:269:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:The seminal work of Myerson and Satterthwaite (1983) demonstrated that, when there is
34:1791:87674:17:17:79:511:252:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:uncertainty about whether gains from trade exist and when a mechanism must be budget-
34:1792:87759:17:17:79:511:235:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:balanced,  any mechanism between one buyer and one seller will fall short of the ex-post
34:1793:87847:17:16:79:510:218:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:efficient outcome.16In used car markets, there is not merely one buyer, but multiple buyers.
34:1794:87939:16:17:79:511:202:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:The natural question then follows:  withN >1 buyers, does the Myerson and Satterthwaite
34:1795:88026:17:17:79:511:185:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(1983) result still hold, or is ex-post efficiency achievable?  Below, we describe the setting
34:1796:88120:17:37:79:511:168:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and data and explain how we apply our menu approach to this setting.  We then discuss
34:1797:88205:37:14:79:511:131:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:14Auctions followed by post-auction bargaining between the buyer and seller have been reported in a number
34:1798:88311:14:11:79:511:117:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:of other settings as well, such as procurement.  In an important precurser to GPV, Elyakime, Laffont, Loisel,
34:1799:88420:11:8:79:351:106:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:and Vuong (1997) analyze this mechanism’s use in timber auctions.
34:1800:88485:8:12:79:511:98:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:15See discussions of complications introduced in these settings in Ausubel, Cramton, and Deneckere (2002).
34:1801:88591:12:15:79:511:86:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:16The ex-post efficient outcome is for trade to occur whenever the buyer values the good more than the
34:1802:88693:15:0:79:102:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:seller.
35:1803:88769:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:counterfactual results,  comparing the mechanism used in practice to the efficient mecha-
35:1804:88858:17:17:79:510:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:nism  forNbuyers  and  1  seller  and  analyzing  how  this  relates  to  Myerson-Satterthwaite
35:1805:88953:17:20:79:134:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:inefficiency.
35:1806:88966:20:17:91:511:634:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:The application we present in this section is related to a previous study focusing on this
35:1807:89056:17:17:79:511:617:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:market, Larsen (2014).  That previous paper also reports welfare measures under counter-
35:1808:89144:17:17:79:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:factual mechanisms, but focuses solely on the post-auction bargaining element of the game,
35:1809:89234:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:whereas here we study instead the fullN-buyer, 1-seller mechanism. That paper also did not
35:1810:89324:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:apply the menu approach we present herein for identification or for estimation, but instead
35:1811:89415:17:17:79:511:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:applied  undominated-strategy  bounds,  akin  to  those  in  Haile  and  Tamer  (2003);  Section
35:1812:89511:17:16:79:511:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:9.3 below highlights the distinction between these types of approaches for other settings.
35:1813:89601:16:17:79:511:516:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Our focus in this section is on applying the menu approach to estimating the distribution
35:1814:89690:17:17:79:511:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of seller valuations given that this is the particularly tricky object to recover structurally,
35:1815:89785:17:17:79:511:482:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:as described below.  Other preliminary steps for estimation are rather straightforward (e.g.
35:1816:89877:17:17:79:511:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:controlling  for  observable  heterogeneity),  and  we  follow  the  same  approach  as  in  Larsen
35:1817:89976:17:17:79:511:448:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(2014)  for  those  preliminary  steps.   We  describe  the  full  estimation  procedure,  including
35:1818:90076:17:36:79:226:431:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:these preliminary steps, below.
35:1819:90107:36:17:79:510:395:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:8.1.Background and Data.The wholesale used-car industry—an industry with revenues
35:1820:90188:17:17:79:511:378:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:above $80 billion annually in the United States—operates through a network of several hun-
35:1821:90278:17:17:79:511:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:dred auction house locations scattered throughout the country (and operations are similar
35:1822:90367:17:17:79:511:344:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:internationally).  These auction houses have been a part of the US used car market for over
35:1823:90458:17:17:79:511:327:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:seventy years.  Over 15 million cars pass through auto auction houses annually.  At each
35:1824:90546:17:16:79:511:310:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:auction house location, used-car dealers come to buy cars from other car dealers or from
35:1825:90634:16:17:79:511:294:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:companies who possess large fleets—such as rental car companies, banks with repossessed
35:1826:90721:17:17:79:511:277:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:vehicles, or manufacturers with lease-buyback vehicles.  Sales at a given auction house typi-
35:1827:90814:17:17:79:511:260:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:cally take place once a week, and the seller of a given car brings the car to the auction house
35:1828:90909:17:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:several days before the sale and reports a secret reserve price to the auction house.  On the
35:1829:91002:17:17:79:511:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:day  of  the  sale,  buyers  (used-car  dealers)  come  to  the  auction  house,  with  many  buyers
35:1830:91102:17:16:79:511:209:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:traveling long distances to attend.  Cars are auctioned off roughly in the order they arrive,
35:1831:91195:16:17:79:511:193:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:with multiple auctions running simultaneously, as multiple sales lanes run throughout the
35:1832:91284:17:21:79:248:176:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:building where the sale takes place.
35:1833:91320:21:16:91:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:The  mechanism  proceeds  as  follows:  buyers  participate  in  an  ascending  auction,  indi-
35:1834:91415:16:17:79:511:139:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:cating their willingness to pay the current price, with the bidding controlled by a human
35:1835:91504:17:17:79:511:122:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:auctioneer who raises the price until only one bidder remains.  The auction itself takes about
35:1836:91598:17:17:79:511:105:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:90 seconds (Lacetera, Larsen, Pope, and Sydnor 2016).  If the final auction price exceeds the
35:1837:91691:17:17:79:511:88:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:secret reserve price (observed to the auctioneer, but not the buyers), then the high bidder is
35:1838:91785:17:0:79:511:71:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:awarded the car.  If not, the high bidder and seller enter into an alternating-offer bargaining
36:1839:91898:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:game, mediated by an auction-house employee over the phone.  The high bidder is allowed
36:1840:91985:17:21:79:391:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the chance to opt out of bargaining before the seller is contacted.
36:1841:92052:21:16:91:511:650:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Our data consists of 133,249 realizations of the auction-plus-bargaining game from sales
36:1842:92140:16:17:79:511:634:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:by fleet/lease sellers (as opposed to sales where the seller was a used-car dealer) from six
36:1843:92232:17:17:79:511:617:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:different auction house locations from 2007–2010.  For each game, the primary variables we
36:1844:92322:17:17:79:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:observe are the seller’s reported secret reserve price,  the final transaction price,  the final
36:1845:92418:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:allocation  (i.e.   an  indicator  for  whether  the  car  sold),  and  the  auction  price.   We  also
36:1846:92521:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:observe a large set of observable characteristics of each sale, including characteristics of the
36:1847:92617:17:17:79:511:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:car and features of the auction house environment at the time of the sale.  Our data also
36:1848:92706:17:42:79:504:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:contains bid logs for a subset of sales, from which the number of bidders can be inferred.
36:1849:92796:42:17:79:511:490:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:8.2.Applying the Menu Approach to Used-Car Markets.To improve clarity,  we
36:1850:92870:17:17:79:511:473:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:will introduce here some notation specific to our application.  The key object of interest for
36:1851:92964:17:17:79:511:456:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:our counterfactual exercises is the distribution of seller private valuations,VS∼FS.  The
36:1852:93053:17:17:79:511:439:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:distribution of buyer valuations,VB∼FB, is also of interest, but Larsen (2014) demonstrates
36:1853:93144:17:16:79:511:422:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that, in this setting, bidders in the auction cannot gain by deviating from truthtelling, and
36:1854:93237:16:17:79:511:406:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:thusFBcan be estimated quite easily using a standard order statistics inversion using the
36:1855:93326:17:17:79:510:389:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:high bid from the auction, a random variable we denoteHB∼FHB.17We assume here that
36:1856:93408:17:17:79:511:372:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:VBandVSare independent and hence, by truthtelling,HBandRwill also be independent.
36:1857:93489:17:17:79:511:355:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:We further assume that the data represents independent realizations of play from a single,
36:1858:93579:17:17:79:511:338:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:position-invariant  equilibrium  of  the  game  (with  the  analytical  characterization  of  that
36:1859:93677:17:20:79:323:321:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium unknown to us as the econometricans).
36:1860:93726:20:17:91:510:301:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:To estimateFS, we apply the results for imperfectly observed actions from Section 4 and
36:1861:93813:17:17:79:511:284:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the results for unobserved heterogeneity from Section 7.2.  Specifically, we will assume that
36:1862:93906:17:17:79:510:267:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the seller’s secret reserve price (a random variableR∼FR) is a strictly increasing function
36:1863:93997:17:16:79:511:250:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of  her  valuationVS—and  thus  serves  as  a  one-to-one  action  shifter—and  that  the  game
36:1864:94092:16:17:79:511:234:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:satisfies the separable heterogeneity property of Section 7.2.  Larsen (2014) demonstrates
36:1865:94182:17:37:79:511:217:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that these two properties will indeed be satisfied in Bayes-Nash equilibria of this game as
36:1866:94273:37:15:79:510:180:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:17N, the number of bidders, varies from one instance of the game to the next.  We assumeNis independent
36:1867:94376:15:16:79:467:165:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:ofVSandVB.  For anyy,FB(y)is estimated by solving the following order-statistic relationship:
36:1868:94469:16:0:186:223:149:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:?:FHB(y) =
36:1869:94477:0:19:225:238:157:9:g_d0_f22:9:g_d0_f22:A:∑
36:1870:94478:19:0:229:234:138:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:A:n
36:1871:94479:0:0:240:281:149:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f8:?:Pr(N=n)
36:1872:94486:0:7:283:287:156:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f21:?:[
36:1873:94487:7:0:287:395:149:9:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f15:?:nFB(y)n−1− (n−1)FB(y)n
36:1874:94509:0:7:396:400:156:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f21:?:]
36:1875:94510:7:23:401:510:149:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:,(22)
36:1876:94515:23:11:79:510:126:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:where  the  distributionFHB(y)is  the  distribution  of  the  high  bid  from  the  auction,  an  estimate  of  which
36:1877:94632:11:11:79:511:115:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:comes the maximum likelihood estimation described below.  Pr(N=n)is the distribution of the number of
36:1878:94733:11:11:79:510:104:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:bidders, which we estimate using the empirical distribution ofNfor the subset of auctions with big log data.
36:1879:94841:11:11:79:511:93:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:See Larsen (2014) for more details on this bid log data and for a proof that the maximum order statistic
36:1880:94945:11:11:79:511:82:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:distribution (which we use in counterfactuals) implied by the estimatedFBand by Pr(N=n)is not sensitive
36:1881:95048:11:0:79:173:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:to the fit of Pr(N=n).
37:1882:95139:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:long as bargaining strategies do not jump discontinuously with the auction price.18We can
37:1883:95228:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:then apply our results to estimate the true menu faced by sellers and,  consequently,  the
37:1884:95318:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium mapping from sellers’ reserve price offers to sellers’ underlying values, given by
37:1885:95412:17:20:79:213:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the derivative of that menu.
37:1886:95440:20:17:91:511:617:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:A:Throughout this section,  for simplicity of exposition,  we will omit the subscripti=S
37:1887:95526:17:17:79:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:from menu objects (P(·),T(·), etc.)  because we only apply the menu approach to estimating
37:1888:95616:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:seller valuations.  We will also omit the( ̆·)notation from menu objects even though these
37:1889:95706:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:will be estimated here using only a partially observable action rather than the seller’s full
37:1890:95799:17:17:79:510:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:B:action vector (which is not observable).  The reserve price functions act an action shifterZ
37:1891:95891:17:20:79:510:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in this application, but for clarity we will simply refer to the reserve price asRthroughout.
37:1892:95984:20:17:91:511:512:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We  first  describe  our  preliminary  estimation  steps  before  we  apply  the  actual  menu
37:1893:96078:17:17:79:511:495:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimation.  Because of the position-invariance property, we can first control for observable
37:1894:96171:17:16:79:511:478:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:heterogeneity through a regression of auction prices and reserve prices onYj,  a large set
37:1895:96261:16:17:79:511:462:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of observables.19We assume this variable enters valuations and actions as a single index,
37:1896:96350:17:17:79:511:445:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:Y′jη, and we estimateηthrough a linear regression.  For the sake of concreteness, we will
37:1897:96439:17:17:79:510:428:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:refer to the predicted value from this regression,Y′jˆη, as the “bluebook” value of the car.
37:1898:96531:17:17:79:511:411:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:We treat the residuals from this regression (that is, reserve prices and auction prices minus
37:1899:96624:17:17:79:511:394:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the bluebook) as contaminated with an unobserved heterogeneity term,W∼FW, which we
37:1900:96706:17:16:79:510:377:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:assume is independent ofVB,VS, andN.  Let these residuals be denoted by the random
37:1901:96788:16:17:79:510:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:variables ̃R=R+Wand ̃HB=HB+W.  We then estimateFW,FR, andFHBby maximum
37:1902:96858:17:21:79:463:344:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:likelihood, as in (16), parameterizing each distribution as a Normal distribution.
37:1903:96940:21:17:91:511:323:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:To apply the menu approach, we then estimate the object ̃P( ̃r)—the noisy measure of the
37:1904:97028:17:16:79:511:306:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:expected allocation function—a using local linear regression ofxjon ̃rjusing a Gaussian
37:1905:97115:16:49:79:511:290:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:kernel.20To  estimate ̃T( ̃r),  we  perform  a  similar  local  linear  regression,  but  where  the
37:1906:97215:49:15:79:511:241:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:18While our estimation relies strongly on the secret reserve price being a one-to-one function of type, even if
37:1907:97326:15:10:79:511:226:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:this assumption is violated, our results in Sections 4.3 and 4.4 suggest that, so long as the setting is relatively
37:1908:97441:10:9:79:476:216:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:smooth, our estimates of value distributions and trade surplus are likely to be close to true values.
37:1909:97542:9:14:79:511:207:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:19The vectorYjcontains fifth-order polynomial terms (all degrees of the polynomial from one through five)
37:1910:97647:14:11:79:511:193:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:in the auction houses’ own bluebook estimate and the odometer reading; the number of previous attempts
37:1911:97749:11:11:79:511:182:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:to sell the car; the number of pictures of the car displayed online on the auction house’s website; a dummy
37:1912:97856:11:11:79:511:171:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:for whether or not the odometer reading is considered accurate,  and the interaction of this dummy with
37:1913:97959:11:11:79:511:160:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:the odometer reading; the interaction of the odometer reading with car-make dummies; dummies for each
37:1914:98060:11:11:79:511:149:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:make-model-year-trim-age combination (where age refers to the age of the vehicle in years);  dummies for
37:1915:98164:11:11:79:511:138:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:condition  report  grade  (ranging  from  1–5);  dummies  for  the  year-month  combination  of  the  date  of  the
37:1916:98279:11:11:79:511:127:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:sale and for auction house location interacted with hour of sale;  dummies for 32 different vehicle damage
37:1917:98385:11:11:79:511:116:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:categories recorded by the auction house; dummies for each seller who appears in at least 500 observations;
37:1918:98492:11:11:79:511:105:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:dummies for discrete odometer bins; and several measures of the thickness of the market during a given sale
37:1919:98599:11:8:79:492:94:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:and of the order the cars were run (see Larsen 2014 for details on the construction of these measures).
37:1920:98702:8:15:79:511:86:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:20We choose a bandwidth of 500 for this estimation.  The mean and standard deviation of reserve prices in
37:1921:98807:15:0:79:211:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:the data are $10,385 and $5,805.
38:1922:98857:0:15:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:dependent variable when trade occurred is the final transaction price minusY′jˆη, denoted,
38:1923:98947:15:23:78:90:673:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B: ̃tj.
38:1924:98952:23:16:91:510:650:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f14:A:Given the estimates ofFR,FW, ̃P( ̃r), and ̃T( ̃r), we solve for the true menu{(P(r),T0(r))}
38:1925:99043:16:17:79:510:634:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:using minimum weighted distance as described in (17) and (18).  ForP(r)we use quadratic
38:1926:99130:17:17:79:511:617:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:splines with 9 knots, constrained to be nondecreasing.  ForT0(r)we use cubic splines with
38:1927:99219:17:17:79:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:7 knots, constrained to be convex.  Finally, since the objectT0(P(r))is represented as a
38:1928:99307:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:convex sum of splines, we can analytically take its derivatives, giving us the final estimated
38:1929:99401:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mapping from reserve prices to valuesvS(r). We then estimate the gains from trade attained
38:1930:99491:17:29:79:501:549:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f4:B:by a seller with valuevSasvSP(r(vS)) −T0(r(vS)), wherer(vS)is the inverse ofvS(r).21
38:1931:99575:29:17:79:511:520:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:8.3.Estimation Results.Before displaying the estimated menu and valuations, we first
38:1932:99659:17:17:79:511:503:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:provide some descriptive evidence that different secret reserve prices do indeed appear to
38:1933:99749:17:17:79:511:486:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:yield different payoffs for sellers, and hence can serve to help separate seller types as a our
38:1934:99844:17:17:79:511:469:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:method requires.  In the left panel of Figure 5 we show the probability of sale as a function
38:1935:99937:17:17:79:511:452:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of sellers’ residualized reserve prices, ̃R.  This probability is estimated from a local linear
38:1936:100032:17:16:79:511:435:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:regression, corresponding to 1− ̃P( ̃r), as ̃P( ̃r)is the probability of the sellerkeepingthe
38:1937:100125:16:17:79:511:419:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:good.   The  units  for  the  horizontal  axis  are  $1,000,  and  these  numbers  can  be  negative
38:1938:100225:17:17:79:511:402:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:because they are the result of subtracting offY′jˆη;  these numbers can thus be thought of
38:1939:100315:17:17:79:510:385:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:indicating where the reserve price lies relative to the bluebook estimate of the car, (Y′jˆη).
38:1940:100409:17:17:79:511:368:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:The right panel of Figure 5 displays, on the vertical axis, the auction price and the final
38:1941:100500:17:17:79:511:351:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:price from the mechanism, again from a local linear regression against reserve prices.22The
38:1942:100591:17:17:79:511:334:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:regressions in each panel use observations with reserve prices lying between the 0.01 and
38:1943:100680:17:20:79:275:317:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:0.99 quantiles of empirical reserve prices.
38:1944:100723:20:17:91:511:297:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Figure  5 demonstrates  that  auction prices  are correlated with  reserve  prices,  violating
38:1945:100817:17:17:79:511:280:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the  independence  assumption  of  the  baseline  model  of  Section  2.   This  suggests  that  it
38:1946:100916:17:16:79:511:263:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is  important  to  account  for  unobserved  heterogeneity  in  this  setting.   We  also  see  that
38:1947:101016:16:17:79:511:247:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sellers who post higher reserve prices sell with lower probabilities,  but are able to attain
38:1948:101109:17:17:79:511:230:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:higher  prices  conditional  on  sale.   In  particular,  the  difference  between  the  average  final
38:1949:101212:17:17:79:511:213:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:price conditional on sale and the average auction price is increasing in the reserve price.
38:1950:101303:17:17:79:511:196:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:The average auction price roughly measures the value of unobserved car-level heterogeneity
38:1951:101393:17:21:79:511:179:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:conditional on the reserve price.23Thus, if the difference between the final price and the
38:1952:101483:21:15:79:511:158:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:21Appendix D describes how computing buyers’ gains from trade requires an additional assumption:  that
38:1953:101585:15:11:79:511:143:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:each seller type trades with all buyer types above a certain cutoff.  Larsen (2014) demonstrates that this
38:1954:101691:11:8:79:511:132:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:property will indeed be satisfied in Bayes-Nash equilibria of this game, relying on results from Storms (2015).
38:1955:101802:8:15:79:511:124:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:22Recall that auction prices and final prices will not necessarily coincide with one another because of the
38:1956:101909:15:11:79:511:109:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:bargaining component of the mechanism.  Also, the final price exists only for observations of the game that
38:1957:102016:11:8:79:294:98:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:end in trade, whereas the auction price always exists.
38:1958:102070:8:17:79:510:90:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:23To see this, note that, since ̃HB=HB+W, ̃R=R+W, andHB,R,Ware mutually independent, we have
38:1959:102162:17:0:79:104:73:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f7:F:thatE
38:1960:102167:0:8:106:110:83:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f21:?:[
38:1961:102168:8:0:112:135:75:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f7:?: ̃HB| ̃R
38:1962:102176:0:10:135:139:83:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f21:A:]
38:1963:102177:10:0:142:156:73:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f7:?:=E
38:1964:102179:0:10:158:162:83:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f21:?:[
38:1965:102180:10:0:162:183:73:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:?:W| ̃R
38:1966:102185:0:10:184:188:83:9:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f21:?:]
38:1967:102186:10:0:190:193:73:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:?:.
39:1968:102256:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:auction  price  is  increasing  in  the  reserve  price,  this  suggests  that  sellers  who  post  high
39:1969:102360:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:reserve prices are forgoing some probability of selling the good in order to obtain a higher
39:1970:102452:17:20:79:126:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sale price.
39:1971:102463:20:17:91:511:634:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:In Figure 6, we show the local linear estimates of ̃P( ̃r), ̃T( ̃r), as well as the unobserved
39:1972:102557:17:17:79:511:617:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:heterogeneity corrected estimatesP(r),T0(r).  We also display intermediate steps in this
39:1973:102645:17:17:79:510:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f8:B:unobserved heterogeneity correction to illustrate the procedure.  For probabilities, the ̃P( ̃r)

39:1975:102832:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:heterogeneity will yield an estimate ofP(r)that is steeper than ̃P( ̃r).  This can be seen in
39:1976:102925:17:17:79:511:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:panel A by comparing theP(r)line to the ̃P( ̃r)line.  For transfers, unobserved heterogene-
39:1977:103016:17:16:79:511:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ity necessitates two corrections to the ̃T( ̃r)function.  First, we subtract from ̃T( ̃r)the term
39:1978:103113:16:17:79:510:516:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:E(W∆P| ̃r),  which  represents  the  expected  value  of  the  unobserved  heterogeneity  condi-
39:1979:103209:17:17:79:510:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tional on ̃r.  Intuitively, for higher values of ̃r, we will observe that trades tend to happen at

39:1981:103395:17:17:79:511:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:on average, rather than the transferT0(r)being higher.  In panel B, comparing the ̃T( ̃r)line

39:1983:103576:17:16:79:510:431:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:transfer function significantly less negative.  Secondly,T0(r)is essentially a noise-corrected
39:1984:103670:16:0:79:168:415:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:B:version of ̃T( ̃r)−E
39:1985:103690:0:12:169:176:427:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:C:(
39:1986:103691:12:0:175:215:415:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:C:W∆ ̃P| ̃r
39:1987:103700:0:12:214:221:427:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:A:)

39:1989:103761:17:17:79:511:398:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:absolute value than the noisy version.  The net effect is thatT0(r)is much less negatively
39:1990:103851:17:17:79:511:381:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sloped—and somewhat more concave—than the original nonparametric estimate ̃T( ̃r).  In
39:1991:103937:17:17:79:511:364:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:each panel, the yellow line displays the convolution of the estimated allocation or transfer

39:1997:104391:17:17:79:511:259:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:menu  corresponds  to  an  expected  payoff  for  the  seller  from  choosing  a  particular  secret
39:1998:104491:17:16:79:511:242:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:reserve price.  We note here that our formulation for payoffs described in (1) in Section 2,

39:2005:105138:16:17:79:511:125:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to the estimated bluebook value of the car,Y′jˆη, so a seller value of -$1,000, for example,
39:2006:105230:17:0:79:385:108:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:represents a seller who values the car at $1,000 below bluebook.
40:2007:105312:0:17:91:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:A:With this interpretation in mind, we compare several points long the menu, markedA–D
40:2008:105396:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in Figure 7.  Each point corresponds to a distinct reserve price, which we will refer to as
40:2009:105487:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:rA–rD, whererA< rB< rC< rD.  PointsAandBlie along the downward-sloping portion
40:2010:105565:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of the menu.  ChoicerAwould yield a lower probability of keeping the good and a lower
40:2011:105650:17:17:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:expected transfer (i.e.  a less negativeT0(r)) than would choicerB.  Therefore, a seller who

40:2013:105830:16:17:79:510:587:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the former seller has a lower value (lowers) than the latter.  This is precisely what Figure 7
40:2014:105924:17:17:79:510:570:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:shows:  the derivative of the menu atrAis more negative than atrB, and these derivatives
40:2015:106012:17:17:79:511:553:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:B:(by Corollary 2) reveal sellers’ values, so a seller choosingrAmust therefore have a values
40:2016:106103:17:17:79:511:536:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that is farther below the bluebook value of the car than does a seller choosingrB.  Points
40:2017:106193:17:17:79:511:519:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:CandDlie along the upward-sloping portion of the menu.  Comparing these two points,

40:2020:106458:17:17:79:511:469:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the good more (i.e.  have a highers) than a seller choosingrC.  This is again clearly revealed
40:2021:106552:17:17:79:511:452:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:B:by the derivatives of the menu at these points:  the derivative is more positive at pointD

40:2031:107385:17:17:79:511:280:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(a value of -1 on the vertical axis).  Therefore, a seller who chooses a reserve price that is
40:2032:107479:17:17:79:511:263:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:$300  below  the  bluebook  is  actually  willing  to  let  the  car  go  for  up  to  $1,000  below  the
40:2033:107584:17:20:79:125:246:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:bluebook.
40:2034:107593:20:17:91:511:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:The estimated reserve-value mapping, combined with the distributionFRof reserve prices,
40:2035:107680:17:17:79:511:209:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:gives us an estimated distributionFSof sellers’ values, and we plot this in panel B of Figure 8.
40:2036:107776:17:17:79:511:192:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:For comparison, we also plot the estimated distribution of the highest-value buyer, which
40:2037:107865:17:17:79:511:175:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is  the  buyer  who  potentially  ends  up  in  bargaining  with  the  seller.24The  distributions
40:2038:107963:17:16:79:511:158:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:indicate that 80% of sellers have values less than about $50 below the bluebook estimate,
40:2039:108052:16:17:79:511:142:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:while nearly 90% of buyers have valuesabovethis amount.  This suggests that there is a
40:2040:108138:17:17:79:511:125:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:lot of room for trade gains in this market, which is to be expected given that these auction
40:2041:108230:17:22:79:511:108:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:houses have been functioning well as market makers in this industry for three quarters of
40:2042:108319:22:15:79:510:86:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:24This distribution can be computed by using the objectsFBand Pr(N=n), described above. The maximum
40:2043:108418:15:0:79:291:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f8:F:order stastic distribution is then given byFB(1)(y) =
40:2044:108471:0:9:293:302:78:9:g_d0_f22:9:g_d0_f22:?:∑
40:2045:108472:9:0:303:382:69:6:g_d0_f15:9:g_d0_f11:?:nPr(N=n)FB(y)n.
41:2046:108556:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a  century.   However,  panel  B  also  shows  overlap  between  seller  and  buyer  distributions,
41:2047:108655:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:which, by the Myerson and Satterthwaite (1983) Theorem, could lead to inefficiency in this
41:2048:108745:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:market  due  to  incomplete  information,  with  some  trades  failing  to  occur  even  when  the
41:2049:108843:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:highest-value  buyer  values  the  good  more  than  the  seller.   We  will  analyze  this  in  more
41:2050:108944:17:20:79:140:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:detail below.
41:2051:108957:20:17:91:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We pause to remark on individual rationality.  Throughout our identification arguments
41:2052:109043:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and estimation process, we have only used localincentive compatibilityconditions of sellers—
41:2053:109135:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that is,  the condition that outcomes under the reserve prices chosen are preferred to the
41:2054:109225:17:17:79:511:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:outcomes from any other possible choice of reserve price.  We have not exploited or enforced
41:2055:109317:17:16:79:511:532:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f5:B:individual rationalityconstraints.  Individual rationality (IR) for the seller refers to the fact
41:2056:109414:16:17:79:511:516:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that the seller should always be able to choose an outcome corresponding to(P,T) = (1, 0);
41:2057:109504:17:17:79:511:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that is, keeping the good with probability 1 and receiving no payment.  There is no simple
41:2058:109594:17:17:79:511:482:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:way to enforce this constraint jointly with our estimation procedure, but it can be imposed
41:2059:109685:17:17:79:511:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:after the fact.  In our estimated menu,  we find that the IR constraint is violated for the
41:2060:109776:17:17:79:511:448:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:roughly  17%  of  seller  types  who  are  inferred  to  have  the  highest  values,  implying  that
41:2061:109876:17:16:79:511:431:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:these sellers would be better off ex-ante by not participating in the mechanism.  Since it
41:2062:109966:16:17:79:511:415:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is empirically implausible that sellers would actually violate individual rationality, in our
41:2063:110059:17:17:79:511:398:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:counterfactual exercise below, we will analyze the mechanism’s efficiency only for the 83%
41:2064:110149:17:17:79:511:381:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of seller types for whom the IR constraint is satisfied.  This is equivalent to assuming that
41:2065:110242:17:17:79:511:364:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:IR-violating sellers have infinitely high values, which is conservative for estimating actual
41:2066:110335:17:17:79:511:347:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and potential gains from trade as it treats these sellers as never having potential gains from
41:2067:110429:17:16:79:511:330:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:trade.  An alternative approach would be to assume that all IR-violating sellers have the
41:2068:110518:16:17:79:511:314:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:same values and expected outcomes as the highest non-IR-violating seller type.  We found
41:2069:110606:17:17:79:511:297:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that taking this approach did not have noticeable effects, qualitatively or quantitatively, on
41:2070:110700:17:40:79:204:280:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:our counterfactual results.
41:2071:110727:40:17:79:511:240:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:8.4.Efficiency,  Optimality,  and Equity.We now compare the outcomes observed in
41:2072:110807:17:17:79:511:223:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the data to a number of counterfactual benchmarks in order to study efficiency, optimality,
41:2073:110898:17:17:79:511:206:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and equity.  These counterfactual benchmarks can each be computed using the estimated
41:2074:110983:17:17:79:511:189:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:distributions  of  valuations.   First,  we  calculate  the  fully  efficient  outcome,  where  trade
41:2075:111084:17:17:79:511:172:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:occurs whenever the highest-value buyer values the good more than the seller.  Second, we
41:2076:111173:17:16:79:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:calculate the the second-best, information-constrained mechanism.  This is the mechanism
41:2077:111261:16:17:79:511:139:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that would maximize ex-ante efficiency in a setting withNbuyers and 1 seller, taking into
41:2078:111350:17:17:79:511:122:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:account players’ incentive compatibility and individual rationality constraints (and budget
41:2079:111441:17:17:79:511:105:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:balance).  This mechanism is similar the second-best mechanism studied in Myerson and
41:2080:111526:17:17:79:511:88:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Satterthwaite  (1983),  but  theirs  is  for  just  1  buyer  and  1  seller.   Appendix  D  discusses
41:2081:111628:17:0:79:511:71:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:technical details of how we solve for this mechanism.  Third,  we consider the mechanism
42:2082:111734:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that would be optimal for the seller in this setting, which is a second-price auction with an
42:2083:111827:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:optimally chosen public reserve price.  Fourth, we consider the buyer-optimal mechanism,
42:2084:111915:17:20:79:450:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in which the highest-value buyer makes a take-it-or-leave-it offer to the seller.
42:2085:111996:20:17:91:511:634:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:These above mechanisms allow us to examine the efficiency of the real-world mechanism
42:2086:112081:17:17:79:511:617:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and its optimality relative to what would be optimal for one-party or the other.  To study
42:2087:112171:17:17:79:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:equity—who obtains what share of the total surplus—we impose no assumptions a priori
42:2088:112255:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:about who has more bargaining power, but instead let the data speak to this question by
42:2089:112342:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:examining the buyer and seller surplus in each of these counterfactual mechanisms and in
42:2090:112430:17:20:79:205:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the real-world mechanism.
42:2091:112455:20:17:91:511:529:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Table 3 displays the welfare measures for each of the counterfactual mechanisms and for
42:2092:112542:17:17:79:511:512:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the real-world mechanism.  Rows 1–4 report each of the four counterfactual mechanisms,
42:2093:112628:17:17:79:511:495:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:followed by the real-world auction-plus-bargaining mechanism in the final row.  For each
42:2094:112716:17:16:79:511:478:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mechanism,  the  first  column  reports  the  probability  of  trade.   Columns  2–6  report  total
42:2095:112815:16:17:79:511:462:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:expected surplus, expected surplus and margin for the seller (seller margin is the difference
42:2096:112908:17:17:79:511:445:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:between the seller’s price and the seller’s value for transacted cars), and expected surplus
42:2097:113000:17:17:79:511:428:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and margin for the highest-value buyer (buyer margin is the difference between the buyer’s
42:2098:113090:17:17:79:511:411:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:value and the price paid for transacted cars).  The final column reports the percentage of
42:2099:113180:17:20:79:241:394:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the surplus achieved by the seller.
42:2100:113215:20:17:91:511:374:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:In terms of surplus division (the final column in Table 3), the mechanism in the data gives
42:2101:113306:17:17:79:511:357:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the seller 60.4% of the trade surplus, slightly lower than the 66.8% that sellers achieve in the
42:2102:113402:17:17:79:511:340:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:second-best mechanism, and lying between the extremes of 41.6% and 76.3% that the seller
42:2103:113490:17:17:79:511:323:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:would  achieve  in  the  buyer-optimal  and  seller-optimal  mechanisms  respectively.   Quanti-
42:2104:113586:17:16:79:511:306:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tatively,  this  implies  that  sellers  achieve  $2,093  of  surplus  in  the  real-world  mechanism,
42:2105:113688:16:17:79:511:290:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:compared to $2,421 in the second-best mechanism, $2,628 in the seller-optimal mechanism,
42:2106:113776:17:17:79:511:273:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and  $1,335  in  the  buyer-optimal  mechanism.   We  can  also  calculate  average  margins  for
42:2107:113873:17:17:79:511:256:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sellers by dividing seller utility by the probability of trade.  This is $2,571 in the real-world
42:2108:113970:17:17:79:511:239:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mechanism, compared to $1,940 in the buyer-optimal mechanism and $3,443 in the seller
42:2109:114055:17:17:79:511:222:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:optimal  mechanism.   Given  that  average  car  prices  are  approximately  $10,000,  this  im-
42:2110:114151:17:16:79:511:205:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:plies that sellers’ markups over their reservation values are approximately 26% of car prices
42:2111:114244:16:17:79:511:189:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in the real-world mechanism,  compared to 19% and 34% at the buyer and seller-optimal
42:2112:114329:17:17:79:511:172:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mechanisms respectively.  Buyer surplus is $1,374 in the real-world mechanism, compared
42:2113:114416:17:17:79:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to  $818  and  $1,874  in  the  seller-optimal  and  buyer-optimal  mechanisms  respectively.   In
42:2114:114514:17:17:79:511:138:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:margin terms, buyers’ margins in the real-world mechanism are roughly 14% of car prices,
42:2115:114602:17:20:79:385:121:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:computed by dividing buyer surplus by the probability of trade.
42:2116:114665:20:17:91:511:101:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:In Figure 9, we display the seller surplus and trade probability specific to different seller
42:2117:114758:17:0:79:511:84:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:types (different valuess) in the real-world mechanism and in each counterfactual mechanism.
43:2118:114918:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Panel A demonstrates that in the real-world mechanism sellers with values near the median
43:2119:115007:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(the  median  seller  value  is  approximately  $78  below  the  bluebook  estimate)  trade  with
43:2120:115104:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:substantially  higher  probabilities  than  in  the  buyer-  and  seller-offer  mechanisms;  sellers
43:2121:115204:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:with values towards the extremes of the distributions trade with probabilities equal to or
43:2122:115294:17:17:79:511:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:lower than the seller-optimal mechanism.  This suggests that sellers with values close to the
43:2123:115387:17:16:79:511:603:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:median contribute significantly to the relatively high efficiency of the real-world auction-
43:2124:115479:16:17:79:511:587:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:plus-bargaining mechanism.  Panel B demonstrates that the real-world mechanism yields
43:2125:115564:17:17:79:511:570:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sellers a surplus that, across most of the range of seller types, is roughly a constant fraction
43:2126:115660:17:17:79:511:553:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of what the seller could achieve in the seller-optimal or the second-best mechanisms.  At
43:2127:115749:17:17:79:511:536:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:seller values closer to the bluebook estimate (i.e.  at seller values closer to 0 on the horizontal
43:2128:115848:17:17:79:511:519:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:axis), the seller-optimal mechanism yields the seller a much higher surplus than in the real-
43:2129:115941:17:20:79:281:502:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:world or second-best efficient mechanisms.
43:2130:115983:20:17:91:511:482:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Returning  to  Table  3,  we  find  that  the  Myerson-Satterthwaite  impossibility  result  for
43:2131:116079:17:17:79:511:465:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:1 buyer and 1 seller—which implies that the second best will always fall short of the first
43:2132:116170:17:17:79:511:448:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:best when buyer and seller distributions overlap—imposes very weak restrictions on feasible
43:2133:116261:17:16:79:511:431:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mechanisms in this context: the maximal possible second-best surplus is 99.99% of the first-
43:2134:116353:16:17:79:511:415:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:best trade surplus.  This is partly because competition between multiple buyers (N >1)
43:2135:116439:17:17:79:511:398:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tends to alleviate Myerson-Satterthwaite impossibility.  In Figure 10, we examine this result
43:2136:116532:17:17:79:511:381:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:more  closely.   We  re-compute  the  second-best  and  first-best  mechanisms  under  different
43:2137:116628:17:17:79:511:364:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:assumptions for the average number of bidders present at the auction, varying this number
43:2138:116717:17:17:79:511:347:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:smoothly  between  between  1  and  2.34,  the  number  estimated  from  bid  log  data.25The
43:2139:116810:17:16:79:511:330:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:upper (blue) line displays the percentage of the first-best surplus achievable in the second-
43:2140:116903:16:17:79:511:314:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:best mechanism, the middle (red) line displays the fraction of first-best sales achieved by
43:2141:116994:17:17:79:511:297:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the second-best mechanism, and the lower (yellow) line displays the percentage of the total
43:2142:117085:17:17:79:511:280:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:surplus sellers achieve in the second-best mechanism.  The plot shows that, as the average
43:2143:117175:17:17:79:511:263:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:number  of  bidders  increases,  the  second-best  achieves  a  larger  fraction  of  the  first-best
43:2144:117276:17:20:79:448:246:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:surplus and sale volume, and sellers attain a larger share of the total surplus.
43:2145:117356:20:17:91:511:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Table  3  also  demonstrates  that  the  auction-plus-bargaining  mechanism  in  the  data  is
43:2146:117450:17:17:79:511:209:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:fairly efficient relative to the second-best,  achieving $3,467 in expected gains from trade,
43:2147:117543:17:17:79:511:192:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:which represents 95.6% of the second-best surplus level, $3,626.  However, the mechanism
43:2148:117631:17:17:79:511:175:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:achieves trade only 81.4% of the time, whereas the second-best mechanism would achieve
43:2149:117717:17:16:79:511:158:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:trade 96.4% of the time.  Interestingly, if the auction house were to employ a mechanism
43:2150:117805:16:17:79:511:142:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that was optimal for either the seller or the buyer, the probability of trade would drop to
43:2151:117896:17:17:79:511:125:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:76.3% and 68.8%, respectively, and the total surplus would drop to $3,445 and $3,209.  This
43:2152:117987:17:22:79:511:108:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:would only be a slight drop in trade or total surplus in the case of the seller mechanism.
43:2153:118077:22:15:79:511:86:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:25We do this by taking convex combinations between the distribution of the number of bidders observed in
43:2154:118181:15:0:79:309:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:the data, and a distribution with a unit mass at 1 buyer.
44:2155:118256:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:The  auction  house  revenue  model  is  such  that  fees  are  paid  only  when  trade  occurs,  so
44:2156:118356:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the  auction  house  cares  particularly  about  keeping  the  probability  of  trade  high.   This
44:2157:118455:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:may explain in part why the auction-plus-bargaining mechanism is used in practice over a
44:2158:118543:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:traditional auction with a reserve price; while the latter would be optimal for the seller, it
44:2159:118637:17:56:79:463:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:would reduce the probability of trade, reducing auction house revenue from fees.
44:2160:118717:56:27:259:330:564:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f6:?:9.Discussion
44:2161:118729:27:16:79:511:537:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:9.1.Counterfactuals.As highlighted in the introduction, a number of counterfactual ex-
44:2162:118815:16:17:79:511:521:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ercises of interest for studying real-world mechanisms involve comparing a mechanism used
44:2163:118904:17:17:79:511:504:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in practice to some theoretical benchmark that achieves some notion of efficiency, optimal-
44:2164:118995:17:17:79:511:487:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ity, equity, no-collusion, efficient collusion, etc.  Or the counterfactual may involve a change
44:2165:119091:17:17:79:511:470:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to an alternative mechanism completely, such as a shift from a median price auction to a
44:2166:119179:17:17:79:511:453:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:first-price auction.  Counterfactuals such as these can be performed using the objects our
44:2167:119269:17:16:79:511:436:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:approach delivers.  Certain types of counterfactuals, however, would not be feasible using
44:2168:119359:16:17:79:511:420:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:our approach.  This includes any counterfactual in which the researcher needs to be able to
44:2169:119450:17:17:79:511:403:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:simulate from the game played in the data and solve for an equilibrium.  For example, in
44:2170:119538:17:17:79:511:386:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:our application to used-car auctions, it would be infeasible to use our approach to study
44:2171:119627:17:17:79:511:369:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the question of what would happen if credit constraints were introduced or if players were
44:2172:119717:17:17:79:511:352:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:required to pay a cost for each bargaining offer made.  Such counterfactuals would require
44:2173:119807:17:16:79:511:335:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:being  able  to  solve  for  equilibria  of  an  alternating-offer  offer  bargaining  game  with  two-
44:2174:119910:16:17:79:511:319:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sided incomplete information (which, as explained above, is beyond the state of the current
44:2175:120001:17:17:79:511:302:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:theory  literature).   Our  approach  explicitly  avoids  modeling  the  game  actually  played  in
44:2176:120100:17:17:79:511:285:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the data, achieving identification of primitives without solving for an equilibrium.  It is an
44:2177:120194:17:17:79:511:268:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f5:B:incomplete  modelapproach.  We see this as a plus for the approach, making it capable of
44:2178:120282:17:17:79:511:251:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:applying to settings where the rules of the game are either unknown or the game’s equilibria
44:2179:120374:17:16:79:511:234:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:are complex, but the approach does indeed rule out studying some counterfactuals that the
44:2180:120463:16:46:79:341:218:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:additional structure of a complete model could deliver.
44:2181:120518:46:17:79:510:172:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:9.2.Beliefs  and  Rational  Expectations.Throughout  this  paper,  we  have  assumed
44:2182:120602:17:16:79:511:155:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Bayes-Nash equilibrium,  which requires that agents have rational expectations about the
44:2183:120690:16:17:79:511:139:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:B:distributions of opposing actions, and thus know the functionsP(a),T(a)for any actiona
44:2184:120776:17:17:79:511:122:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that they could play.  This assumption is important for our estimation procedure; if agents’
44:2185:120868:17:17:79:510:105:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:beliefs coincide with the true conditional expectationsP(a),T(a), we can simply estimate
44:2186:120956:17:17:79:511:88:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:agents’ beliefs using expected outcome functions in data.  Our approach is in fact robust to
44:2187:121048:17:0:79:511:71:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:some deviations from Bayes-Nash equilibrium:  since only agenti’s best response condition
45:2188:121206:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:B:is used to estimate her valuation, inference about agenti’s value only requires that agenti
45:2189:121297:17:21:79:453:671:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f4:B:has correct beliefs about opponents’ actions, not that all agents are rational.26
45:2190:121378:21:16:91:511:650:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Our approach can fail for agents who do not have correct beliefs about the distribution
45:2191:121465:16:14:79:511:634:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of opponents’ actions.  These agents can be thought of as optimizing with respect to some
45:2192:121554:14:20:80:510:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B: ̇P(a), ̇T(a)functions  which  may  differ  from  empirical  averages,  and  the  econometrician
45:2193:121650:20:17:79:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:must then take an essentially unverifiable stance on how agents’ ̇P(a), ̇T(a)functions are
45:2194:121740:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:formed. A number of approaches have been proposed in the literature. Agarwal and Somaini
45:2195:121828:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(2018) estimate values assuming rational expectations as well as coarse and lagged expec-
45:2196:121917:17:17:79:511:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tations.  Syrgkanis, Tamer, and Ziani (2017) explore inference in auctions under different
45:2197:122007:17:16:79:511:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:information assumptions.  In a related literature, Doraszelski, Lewis, and Pakes (2018) show
45:2198:122099:16:17:79:511:516:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that firms in a new market for frequency response behave in a way that is more consistent
45:2199:122188:17:21:79:376:499:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:with adaptive learning than rational-expectations equilibrium.
45:2200:122250:21:16:91:511:478:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Belief  formation  in  multi-agent  games  is  a  difficult  and  important  question  in  the  lit-
45:2201:122350:16:17:79:511:462:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:erature;  further discussion is beyond the scope of this paper,  but we emphasize that the
45:2202:122440:17:17:79:511:445:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:assumption of rational expectations is important for our methods to work.  This may be
45:2203:122526:17:17:79:511:428:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a reasonable assumption for marketplace-like settings, in which traders interact frequently
45:2204:122617:17:17:79:511:411:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in  environments  that  are  relatively  stationary  over  time,  but  it  may  be  less  appropriate
45:2205:122718:17:17:79:511:394:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:for large one-shot mechanisms, or nonstationary settings in which agents are learning and
45:2206:122807:17:34:79:306:377:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:converging towards optimal behavior over time.
45:2207:122853:34:17:79:511:343:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f13:B:9.3.Belief Estimation versus Undominated-Strategy Approaches to Identifica-
45:2208:122928:17:17:79:510:326:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f5:B:tion.This  paper,  along  with  GPV  and  many  of  the  papers  discussed  in  the  subsection
45:2209:123023:17:17:79:511:309:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:above,  assumes  that  agents  are  optimizing  with  respect  to  some  beliefs  about  outcomes,
45:2210:123121:17:17:79:511:292:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and moreover that the econometrician can estimate these beliefs.  If these beliefs can be
45:2211:123210:17:16:79:511:275:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimated, revealed preference arguments can be applied to identify agents’ values.  We view
45:2212:123302:16:17:79:511:259:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:these papers as conceptually distinct from a set of identification and estimation approaches
45:2213:123394:17:17:79:511:242:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that are based instead on the concept ofrationalizability, orundominated  strategies.  Ex-
45:2214:123484:17:17:79:511:225:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:amples include Haile and Tamer (2003) (or recent work by Chesher and Rosen (2017)) for
45:2215:123570:17:17:79:511:208:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:estimating bounds on buyer valuations in ascending auctions or Larsen (2014) for estimat-
45:2216:123659:17:17:79:511:191:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ing bounds on seller valuations in bargaining games.  Rather than taking a stance on what
45:2217:123748:17:16:79:511:174:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:agents’ beliefs about outcomes are, these approaches rule out only values under which ac-
45:2218:123837:16:17:79:511:158:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tions observed in the data are dominated—that is, values for which particular actions could
45:2219:123928:17:17:79:511:141:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:not to be rationalizable byanybelief.  In the classic example of Haile and Tamer (2003),
45:2220:124016:17:27:79:510:124:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:an agent bidding some amountyat some point in an ascending auction must have value
45:2221:124098:27:15:79:511:97:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:26A similar argument is made in Nekipelov, Syrgkanis, and Tardos (2015), who argue that many learning
45:2222:124199:15:11:79:511:82:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:algorithms should eventually converge to regret-free behavior, which motivates using no-regret conditions—
45:2223:124305:11:0:79:478:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:essentially best-response conditions for stationary averages over opponents’ actions—in estimation.
46:2224:124422:0:17:79:510:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f7:B:abovey; if not, there is no possible outcome that the agent could achieve from biddingy
46:2225:124509:17:21:79:277:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:that would give the agent positive utility.
46:2226:124552:21:16:91:511:650:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:The belief estimation approach requires strictly stronger assumptions about agents’ be-
46:2227:124639:16:17:79:511:634:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:liefs  than  the  rationalizability-based  approach;  if  the  econometrician  is  willing  to  make
46:2228:124739:17:17:79:511:617:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:these assumptions, the benefit can be powerful identification results with weaker assump-
46:2229:124828:17:17:79:511:600:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tions about game structure.  In contrast to rationalizability-based approaches such as Haile
46:2230:124920:17:17:79:511:583:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and Tamer (2003), the approach we take here allows the econometrician to use essentially
46:2231:125008:17:17:79:511:566:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:no information about the rules of the game;  all relevant information about game rules is
46:2232:125097:17:17:79:511:549:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:inferred from observing game outcomes.  Moreover, rationalizability-based approaches tend
46:2233:125186:17:16:79:511:532:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to only allow partial identification of values, whereas our approach can often achieve point
46:2234:125278:16:21:79:144:516:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:identification.
46:2235:125293:21:17:91:511:495:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:We believe that these two approaches can be used in a complementary manner.  In some
46:2236:125377:17:16:79:511:478:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:settings, for example, dominance-based arguments could be used to robustly find bounds
46:2237:125463:16:17:79:511:462:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:on agents’ values,  and the stronger assumption of Bayes-Nash equilibrium could be used
46:2238:125550:17:33:79:274:445:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:more tentatively to point-identify values.
46:2239:125592:33:17:79:511:412:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:9.4.Multiple Equilibria.We assume that agents are playing a single equilibrium across
46:2240:125677:17:17:79:511:395:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:all observations.  In some marketplace-like settings, agents interact with anonymous trading
46:2241:125769:17:17:79:511:378:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:partners and few observables are available for agents to coordinate on; the assumption that
46:2242:125860:17:17:79:511:361:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:all  agents  are  playing  the  same  equilibrium  may  be  plausible  in  these  settings.   In  other
46:2243:125963:17:17:79:511:344:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:settings,  agents  may  be  able  to  coordinate  to  play  different  equilibria  based  on  various
46:2244:126064:17:17:79:511:327:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:features  of  the  environment  that  they  observe.   For  example,  in  timber  auctions,  agents
46:2245:126163:17:16:79:511:310:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:bidding  in  auctions  for  high  quality  timber  could  play  a  certain  equilibrium,  bidding  in
46:2246:126264:16:17:79:511:294:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a systematically different way than agents bidding in auctions for low quality timber.  In
46:2247:126354:17:17:79:511:277:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:such settings, if the econometrician observes all possible characteristics that agents could
46:2248:126446:17:17:79:511:260:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:use for coordination, the problem of multiple equilibria could be addressed by estimating
46:2249:126535:17:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:equilibrium menus conditional on observables, rather than pooling all observations into a
46:2250:126624:17:17:79:511:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:single menu.  This effectively allows a different equilibrium to be played for each possible
46:2251:126716:17:16:79:511:209:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:combination of observables characterizing a trading game.  There may be setting in which
46:2252:126804:16:17:79:511:193:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:agents play different equilibria conditional on variables unobserved by the econometrician;
46:2253:126895:17:17:79:511:176:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:this  presents  an  interesting  unobservable  heterogeneity  problem  for  which  we  do  not  yet
46:2254:126994:17:20:79:154:159:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:have a solution.
46:2255:127010:20:17:91:511:139:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Examples of features on which equilibrium selection can depend would be a reserve price
46:2256:127097:17:17:79:511:122:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in an auction or the number of competing bidders in an auction.  If reserve prices are present
46:2257:127191:17:17:79:511:105:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and vary from one instance of the game to the next, and if these reserve prices are observable
46:2258:127285:17:17:79:511:88:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to agents, the econometrician would also need to observe and condition on reserve prices in
46:2259:127376:17:0:79:511:71:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:order to correctly estimate equilibrium menus for buyers.  Similarly, if agents can observe
47:2260:127536:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:the  number  of  their  competitors  and  this  number  affects  equilibrium  behavior  (it  would
47:2261:127634:17:17:79:511:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:do so in a first-price auction, for example, but not in an ascending button auction), then
47:2262:127724:17:17:79:511:654:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:econometrician should observe and condition on this quantity when estimating equilibrium
47:2263:127812:17:17:79:511:637:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:menus.  If, however, agents themselves do not observe the number of their competitors, the
47:2264:127902:17:33:79:432:620:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:econometrician need not observe it either in applying the menu approach.
47:2265:127974:33:17:79:510:587:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:9.5.Affine-Utility Games.We focus in this paper on trading games,  in which agents’
47:2266:128057:17:17:79:511:570:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:utility  functions  depend  on  an  indicator  variablexifor  trade  and  real-valued  transfers
47:2267:128153:17:16:79:510:553:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:ti.  However, our arguments only utilize the fact that agents’ expected utilities are affine
47:2268:128245:16:17:79:511:537:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:functions of expected outcomes, up to some unknown vector of types, and similar arguments
47:2269:128334:17:17:79:511:520:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:apply to other settings in which agents maximize objective functions which are affine in types
47:2270:128428:17:21:79:201:503:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:and observable outcomes.
47:2271:128452:21:16:91:511:482:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:For  example,  in  an  oligopolistic  competition  setting,  our  menu  estimation  approach  is
47:2272:128548:16:17:79:511:466:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:related to the Baker and Bresnahan (1988) approach of using firm cost shifters to estimate
47:2273:128638:17:17:79:511:449:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:theresidual  demand  curvefacing a given firm,  and using this to make statements about
47:2274:128725:17:17:79:511:432:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:firms’  price-setting  power.   Similar  arguments  apply  to  other  settings  in  which  firms  or
47:2275:128825:17:17:79:511:415:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:agents  have  preferences  that  are  assumed  to  be  linear  in  some  quantity  measureq(p),
47:2276:128920:17:17:79:511:398:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:rather than a probabilityP(a)as in our setting.27Applying our approach to such settings
47:2277:129007:17:16:79:511:381:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:could allow for firms to potentially have incomplete information about competitors’ costs
47:2278:129096:16:17:79:511:365:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:without assuming a particular model of conduct by those firms.  This could be particularly
47:2279:129186:17:17:79:511:348:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:useful given that Sweeting, Tao, and Yao (2018) point out that small amounts of asymmetric
47:2280:129276:17:17:79:511:331:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:information in oligopoly pricing can have big effects on prices, and price setting in such cases
47:2281:129372:17:20:79:394:314:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:may look similar to collusion if incomplete information is ignored.
47:2282:129439:20:17:91:511:294:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:Related arguments also apply to settings in which agents maximize affine functions of
47:2283:129524:17:17:79:511:277:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:more than two outcomes.  Agarwal and Somaini (2018) analyze school choice problems, in
47:2284:129610:17:17:79:511:260:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:which applicants’ utilities for submitting a given report are affine functions of probabilities
47:2285:129705:17:17:79:511:243:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of admission to different schools, and uses this to derive identification and estimation argu-
47:2286:129799:17:17:79:511:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ments.  Gentry, Komarova, and Schiraldi (2014) use similar arguments to analyze bidding
47:2287:129886:17:16:79:511:209:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:in combinatorial auctions for highway procurement.  While our nonparametric estimation
47:2288:129972:16:17:79:511:193:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is specialized to the case of two outcomes,  menus are also convex in settings with multi-
47:2289:130062:17:17:79:511:176:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ple goods,  and similar approaches to ours can be applied in such settings.  For example,
47:2290:130151:17:17:79:511:159:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Agarwal and Somaini (2018) show that solving for agents’ values for any preference report
47:2291:130240:17:26:79:511:142:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:requires satisfying a set of revealed-preference inequalities that define the subgradient set
47:2292:130333:26:14:79:511:116:8:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f11:F:27For example, consider a monopolist pricing problem, where the monopolist chooses pricepto maximize
47:2293:130433:14:15:79:511:102:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f11:F:pq(p)−cq(p), wherecis the (potentially privately known) marginal cost andq(p)is demand.  Defining
47:2294:130530:15:0:79:412:87:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f11:F:T(p)=pQ(p),  we  can  write  monopolist  profit  asT(p)−cq(p)and  obtaincas
47:2295:130605:0:10:419:428:95:5:g_d0_f30:5:g_d0_f30:?:dTdp
47:2296:130609:10:14:419:510:85:5:g_d0_f30:9:g_d0_f11:F:dqdp=c,  which  can  be
47:2297:130632:14:0:79:390:71:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:F:re-written to obtain the standard monopolist pricing formulac=p+qp′(q).
48:2298:130721:0:17:79:511:688:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of a multidimensional convex function; this is a linear programming problem, so it is fairly
48:2299:130813:17:27:79:273:671:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:straightforward even in high dimensions.
48:2300:130853:27:17:79:511:644:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:9.6.Mechanism  Design.The  class  of  quasilinear-utility  trading  games  that  we  study
48:2301:130943:17:17:79:511:627:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:here is exactly the canonical model of classical mechanism design, as pioneered by Myerson
48:2302:131033:17:17:79:511:610:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(1981),  and  many  parallels  can  be  drawn  between  our  results  and  this  literature.   Simi-
48:2303:131133:17:16:79:511:593:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:larly to the mechanism design literature, our incentive compatibility constraints in (1) rely
48:2304:131226:16:17:79:511:577:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:only  on  the  quasilinear-utility  setup,  and  are  independent  of  the  particular  game  being
48:2305:131325:17:17:79:511:560:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:played.  Indeed, one interpretation of our results from the perspective of mechanism design
48:2306:131416:17:17:79:511:543:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:is that equilibria of arbitrary trading games can alternatively be thought of as revelation
48:2307:131507:17:17:79:511:526:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:mechanisms,  in  which  the  abstract  actions  that  agents  take  are  their  type  reports.   The
48:2308:131607:17:17:79:511:509:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:econometrician can estimate the mapping that the revelation mechanism from type reports
48:2309:131694:17:16:79:511:492:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to outcomes, and use this to estimate the value of an agent making any given type report.
48:2310:131783:16:17:79:511:476:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:The constraint that equilibrium menus are convex is related to the implementability con-
48:2311:131871:17:17:79:511:459:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:straint  from  Myerson,  stating  that  equilibrium  allocations  must  be  weakly  increasing  in
48:2312:131969:17:17:79:511:442:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:types.  The “empirical ironing” procedures we propose in Section 5 to enforce menu con-
48:2313:132056:17:17:79:511:425:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:vexity are thus related to the concept of ironing demand curves to enforce monotonicity of
48:2314:132146:17:29:79:337:408:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:optimal allocation rules in optimal mechanism design.
48:2315:132199:29:27:254:336:379:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f6:?:10.Conclusion
48:2316:132212:27:17:91:511:352:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:This  paper  provides  a  two-step  identification  argument,  based  on  intuitions  from  the
48:2317:132307:17:17:79:511:335:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:theoretical mechanism design literature, for general incomplete information trading games,
48:2318:132397:17:17:79:511:318:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:generalizing a number of game-specific approaches in the literature.  We propose an method
48:2319:132487:17:17:79:511:301:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:to deal with imperfectly observed actions, derive general estimation procedures, and extend
48:2320:132578:17:16:79:511:284:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:tools for unobserved heterogeneity and correlated private values from auctions setting to
48:2321:132667:16:17:79:511:268:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:general trading games.  We believe our results may be useful in a number of incomplete-
48:2322:132754:17:17:79:511:251:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:information settings where closed-form equilibrium solutions may not exist, or where play-
48:2323:132844:17:17:79:511:234:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ers’ actions may be difficult to fully observe, or where the rules of the game are not neces-
48:2324:132937:17:17:79:511:217:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:sarily known to the econometrician, such as incomplete-information sequential bargaining
48:2325:133025:17:0:79:111:200:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:games.
49:2326:133100:0:24:263:327:688:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:?:References

68:3559:160143:44:26:173:416:627:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:?:AppendixC.Bargaining Simulation Details
68:3560:160182:26:17:91:511:601:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:For the bargaining simulations, we follow the game studied in Satterthwaite and Williams
68:3561:160270:17:17:79:511:584:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:(1989), referred to as akdouble auction.  The authors demonstrated that, for anyk∈[0, 1],
68:3562:160359:17:17:79:511:567:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:a  continuum  of  strictly  increasing,  differentiable  equilibria  exist  satisfying  the  following
68:3563:160461:17:17:79:510:550:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:linked differential equations for the buyer’s actionaBand seller’s actionaSas a function
68:3564:160549:17:26:79:309:533:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of their private valuationsVB∼FBandVS∼FS:
68:3565:160590:26:0:146:312:507:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f8:C:a(−1)B(aS(vS)) =aS(vS) +ka′S(vS)
68:3566:160622:0:15:314:322:522:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:C:(
68:3567:160623:15:0:322:344:507:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f8:A:vS+
68:3568:160626:0:15:348:379:514:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f8:C:FS(vS)
68:3569:160632:15:0:348:378:499:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f8:C:fS(vS)
68:3570:160638:0:15:380:388:522:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:A:)
68:3571:160639:15:32:390:510:507:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:,(32)
68:3572:160644:32:0:145:342:475:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f8:C:a(−1)S(aB(vB)) =aB(vB) + (1−k)a′B(vB)
68:3573:160681:0:16:344:352:491:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:C:(
68:3574:160682:16:0:352:375:475:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f8:A:vB−
68:3575:160685:0:15:379:430:483:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f8:A:1−FB(vB)
68:3576:160693:15:0:389:421:468:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f8:A:fB(vB)
68:3577:160699:0:16:432:440:491:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:C:)
68:3578:160700:16:27:442:510:475:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:.(33)
68:3579:160705:27:17:79:511:448:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:Satterthwaite and Williams (1989) provided an approach for solving for equilibria numer-
68:3580:160793:17:17:79:511:431:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:ically  given  knowledge  of  the  distributions  of  player  types.    A  point(vS,vB,t),  where
68:3581:160890:17:16:79:511:414:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:tis  a  final  price  whichvSandvBcould  potentially  agree  upon,  is  chosen  in  the  set
68:3582:160982:16:17:79:511:398:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f5:B:P={(vS,vB,t) :vS6vS6t6vB6vB,vS6vS,vB>vB}, and then a one-dimensional
68:3583:161050:17:17:79:511:381:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:manifold passing through this point is traced out using the differential equations defined
68:3584:161140:17:17:79:511:364:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:by (32) and (33).  This path traces out an equilibrium.  This approach does not allow for
68:3585:161229:17:17:79:511:347:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:identification of players’ value distributions, only for solving for equilibria given knowledge
68:3586:161324:17:17:79:511:330:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:of the distributions.  We use their approach to solve for an equilibrium and simulate data
68:3587:161414:17:20:79:497:313:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:from equilibrium play, then apply our method for estimating the underlying valuations.
68:3588:161500:20:17:91:511:293:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:A:In our bargaining simulations, we focus on two possibilities for valuation distributions:
68:3589:161589:17:17:79:511:276:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f5:B:VS∼U[0, 1]andVB∼U[0, 1], orVS∼N(.2, .5)andVB∼N(.6, .3).  For the Normal case, we
68:3590:161669:17:17:79:510:259:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:truncate the distribution to lie within[0, 1]to simplify computation. We setk=1/2. In each
68:3591:161759:17:16:79:511:242:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:case we choose an equilibrium passing through the point(vS,vB,t) = (0.375, 0.625, 0.5).  An
68:3592:161850:16:17:79:511:226:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:example of a solution path crossing through this point, for the truncated Normal case, is
68:3593:161939:17:44:79:173:209:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:B:shown in Figure 12.
